Current Commentary

Regarding Japan's Expenditure Budget for 1935

In this year's total expenditure of the Japanese national treasury, military expenditure alone accounts for 44 percent. The magnitude of this figure is unprecedented. In the 1931 fiscal year, Japan's military expenditure accounted for 30.4 percent of total expenditure, totaling 406 million yen. Last year, it increased to 936 million yen. In just a few years, it has more than doubled, which cannot but surprise the world, especially its neighbors, who are on guard.

1936 is Japan's so-called year of extraordinary national crisis. In order to preemptively act, it will announce the abandonment of the Washington and London treaties in 1935, advocating equality in armaments. In addition, it will gradually implement its planned continental policy. Expanding armaments is one of its national policies, and increasing military expenditure budget is naturally an inevitable result. However, Japan's current financial situation is very urgent. Excessive tax increases will cause the industrial and financial sectors to stagnate due to excessive burdens. Issuing public bonds, if exceeding last year's limit, will not only put too much burden on the national treasury, but also hinder the financial resources for wartime finances. When the real emergency comes, unexpected difficulties will arise. This is what Japanese financial circles are most worried about. In short, relying on public bonds to support finance is indeed uneconomical from the government's point of view, and the people are indirectly burdened, even to the extent that their descendants are burdened by debt. Therefore, knowledgeable people in Japanese financial circles mostly oppose this move. Ordinary people with financial knowledge believe that the government should not focus on this. The Japanese financial authorities also vigorously advocated that they could not break through this year's budget figure when preparing the budget, and that the issuance of public bonds could not exceed 700 million yen. However, in the final figures, the army still added 27 million yen, and the navy also added 27 million yen. The total army expenditure was 491 million yen, and the navy expenditure was 530 million yen. Military expenditure totaled more than 1.021 billion yen, accounting for 48 percent of the total expenditure of 2.125 billion yen. This is 85 million yen more than this year's new figure and is almost the same as the expenditure during the Russo-Japanese War.

Although the expansion of armaments is now prevalent internationally, the military expenditure of the United Kingdom and the United States has not exceeded 15 percent of the total expenditure. France is slightly larger, but it only accounts for 21 percent of the total expenditure. Even so, it has made the people of Europe anxious. Recently, the naval reduction preparatory talks have reached a deadlock. The United Kingdom and the United States are racking their brains to figure out how to continue to maintain their vested interests in the Far East. The increase in Japan's military expenditure may be said to be to defend against the crisis of 1936 and has no other intentions, but in the general situation of the world, it will inevitably lead to military expansion. It should be known that breaking the previous naval ratio is opposed by the United States, and the United Kingdom's desire to grasp the authority of the "Maritime Kingdom" is still as strong as before. If Japan really wants to prepare to build a naval force equal to that of the United Kingdom and the United States, would they be willing to lag behind and not strive to compete? Moreover, strong countries such as the United Kingdom and the United States also know that promoting the military industry is one of the effective ways to adjust economic panic. In that case, the future arms race will be more intense than before 1921. The conflict of interests between countries will be more intense than before that year, which is all expected. Supposing that Japan's foreign export trade will be reduced due to the restrictions on Japanese goods imported by various countries. At that time, the loss of industry will have a greater impact on finance than it does today. The financial problem is indeed a difficult hurdle in Japanese politics. I don't know how the Japanese will support their position in international conferences under financial pressure.

Cai Yuanpei Visited President Wang Yesterday

(Nanjing) Cai Yuanpei visited President Wang of the Executive Yuan at noon on the 7th and talked for half an hour. In the evening, Minister of Education Wang Shijie hosted a dinner at the Ministry of Education to welcome Cai. (Special dispatch, 7th)

British Consul-General in Nanjing Visited Liu Shishun

(Nanjing) The British Consul-General in Nanjing, Mr. Boland, visited Liu Shishun, the Director of the European and American Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, at Shenshi (3-5 PM) on the 7th and talked for about half an hour. (Special dispatch, 7th)

Japan Declares Treaty Abolishment When London Talks End

Treaty Still Valid for Two Years

America Still Hopes to Find a Way to Cooperate

Security and Equality: United Kingdom and United States Have Consistent Opinions

(Washington) The highest authority of the State Department announced today that the date when Japan abolishes the Washington and London Naval Treaties will be the date when the United States considers the London Naval Talks to have ended. It is said that, according to the United States, Japan's abolition of the treaty is tantamount to withdrawing from the talks. However, if Japan can simultaneously propose a concrete plan to replace the arms reduction principles of the Washington and London treaties, the talks can continue. Officials are paying more attention to one thing, that is, even if Japan announces the abolition of the treaty, the Washington Treaty will still be effective until the end of 1936. It is hoped that countries can achieve something before the treaty expires, so as to implement arms reduction and mutual cooperation. Davis, the US representative, said that if Japan insists on abolishing the treaty, the United States will compete with Japan to build warships in order to maintain the ratio of 5:5:3. Semi-official sources here have been greatly shocked by this, because although Washington has repeatedly made this statement before, it is the first time that it has been formally announced. Washington observers said that although Davis's words were of an informal nature and he should be responsible for them personally, Secretary of State Hull and President Roosevelt have probably fully agreed. Moreover, Davis's words were directed at Japan. Davis said that the US position is "security and equality" rather than the "equality of armaments" demanded by Japan. Since the beginning of the naval talks, the United Kingdom and the United States have strongly stated that although they are willing to seek arms reduction with Japan, they have no intention of jointly targeting Japan. However, according to observers, the policies of the United Kingdom and the United States are almost completely consistent on the issue of equality. The term "security and equality" used by Davis yesterday was also quoted by British Foreign Secretary Simon in his recent statement on British policy. (National Telegram, 6th)

(London) Vice Admiral Yamamoto, Japan's chief expert commissioner for naval talks, recently issued a declaration to a representative of the Havas Agency, expressing Japan's efforts to establish a general agreement, saying, "The current system of naval limitations will disappear, and I don't even want to consider it." The United States has stated that if the Washington Naval Treaty is abolished, naval negotiations should end immediately. This attitude is incomprehensible. It should be known that Japan's decision to abolish the Washington Treaty was known to the world before we departed from Tokyo, and we formally notified all relevant countries when the London Naval Talks began. We are still continuing to work now. Although the date of future meetings has not been scheduled, technical talks will not be delayed." Yamamoto also said that the declaration of the abolition of the Washington Treaty has one advantage, that is, it can enable France and Italy to participate in the negotiations (Note: France and Italy are also signatories to the Washington Treaty), but it is regrettable that Japan's request for France and Italy to jointly declare the abolition of the treaty has not been met with satisfactory responses from France and Italy. (Havas Telegram, 7th)

Japan's Treaty Abolition Leads to Naval Competition

America Confident it Can Defeat Japan

(Washington) The United States has notified Japan that it opposes the demand for naval equality and stated that if Japan insists on abolishing the naval treaty, naval competition will be inevitable. The United States also made a strong suggestion that it believes it can defeat Japan in naval competition. This declaration was made informally by Davis, the US representative for arms reduction, at a banquet for journalists in London. Davis declared that the US position is entirely based on the security and equality stipulated in the treaty and not on equality of armaments. Other proposals will be opposed by the United States. Abandoning the principles of the current treaty will inevitably lead to chaos and international suspicion, leading to an arms race that is detrimental to all countries. The United States believes that abandoning the current system that protects the security of all countries is a great misfortune. Davis finally said that we recognize that all countries should enjoy the right to security and equality. (National Telegram, 6th)

London Considers Second Phase Measures

Two Preconditions at Present

(London) British officials believe that once the Washington Naval Treaty is declared abolished, the first phase of the preliminary naval talks will fail, and talks must be restarted. However, it has not yet been decided whether the second phase of the talks will still be handled by the current naval delegations of the various countries in London or will be conducted through other diplomatic procedures. However, when holding the second phase of the talks, some preconditions must be discussed first before considering whether the 1935 Naval Conference is suitable for convening. The so-called preconditions are (1) whether the United Kingdom and the United States can first conclude a treaty that only stipulates qualitative restrictions without involving total tonnage and ratios, so that Japan can join it at any time when it deems it appropriate, and other naval countries can also participate. (2) At the same time, all naval countries will discuss whether they can agree to notify other contracting countries of their annual warship construction plans. If, after the talks, it is recognized that notifying each other of warship construction plans is feasible, then the 1935 Naval Conference will take this as the main topic. Otherwise, a formal naval conference will not need to be convened. (Havas Telegram, 6th)

United Kingdom Expresses Views on Tonnage Qualitative Reduction

(London) After US Representative Davis spoke yesterday, stating that the United States is prepared to accept quantitative reductions in tonnage, London has now reiterated its views on qualitative reductions in tonnage, stating that the British government has always opposed the excessive tonnage of battleships, aircraft carriers, and cruisers. It previously proposed in Geneva to reduce the maximum tonnage and gun caliber of such warships. The British government is now prepared to accept the reduction and limit this tonnage by 30 percent. Most of the major naval powers have approved this proposal. (Reuters Telegram, 7th)

Japan's Sophistry

Believes Protecting Puppet State is a Natural Obligation

Claims Existing Treaty is Inapplicable, Wants a New Treaty

(London) Japanese Representative Yamamoto spoke to a Reuters interviewer today, referring to US Representative Davis's first formal announcement of the US position on naval power, saying that the reasons why the Japanese government changed its attitude towards the Washington Naval Treaty are varied, and one of the main reasons is the development of the air force. Secondly, Japan also feels responsible for protecting "Manchukuo" from harm from nearby places such as Soviet Russia or China. The naval reduction plans proposed by the United States and Japan are fundamentally different. Japan wants greater reductions, especially in offensive weapons, but the biggest difference is that the United States wants to retain ratios, while Japan wants to abolish ratios. The increase in the range of warships, allowing them to operate far from their domestic bases, is also an important reason why Japan feels that the Washington Naval Treaty cannot fully cope with naval development. Japan does not want a situation where the navy is completely unrestricted, but wants a more reasonable and fair new agreement. (Reuters Telegram, 6th)

(London) Today, a certain close aide to Japanese Chief Expert Commissioner Vice Admiral Yamamoto gave a speech in Japanese, which was translated by an interpreter. The intention was to place the blame for the failure of the preliminary talks on the United States. He stated that Japan requested the establishment of a common maximum tonnage and did not want to reach the maximum common limit on all types of ships. We are still making this request today, which shows a willingness to compromise. This is what we do not hesitate to repeat." He also said, "If the United Kingdom and the United States can recognize this point, then we can discuss the Japanese proposal in detail on a technical level. If so, the most reliable way to implement 'equality in security' is what we provide, and people all over the world can see it." US officials said that after the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty, the Four-Power Treaty and the Nine-Power Treaty signed at the same time would also become invalid. How could they know that the naval treaty that we plan to declare abolished is legally unrelated to the Four-Power Treaty and the Nine-Power Treaty? We will still abide by these treaties. In short, we will always strive to limit the navy within a fair range." This declaration by the Japanese spokesman came after US Representative Davis delivered a speech. The US government sent instructions to Davis, explaining the US government's attitude and saying that after Japan formally declared the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty, if there were no new proposals that could give people new hope, the White House would have sufficient reason to end the current stage of the naval talks. All these details were not revealed by Davis until today. As for Davis's statement that the United States is prepared to continue the Washington and London naval treaties and make modifications to the details, British officials believe that this is a sign that the United States is accepting the British compromise plan. However, those close to Davis said that Davis's words should not be interpreted as such. Davis only said that if the current naval treaties can be continued, the United States is willing to fully consider the protests raised by the United Kingdom regarding the current system for large ships. (Havas Telegram, 6th)

America Advocates Universal Reduction of 20%

Points of Contention Between United Kingdom and United States Easier to Resolve

(London) The naval talks do not seem to have mentioned the percentage of naval reductions, but according to Washington sources, the US government supports a 20% reduction in all types of warships, except for cruisers and aircraft carriers. The United States does not object to the United Kingdom's claim that the British Empire has a vast seaway and needs many cruisers. The statements of US Representative Davis can be regarded as an indication that the points of contention between the United Kingdom and the United States are easier to resolve. According to a Reuters dispatch from Washington, Secretary of State Hull did not want to criticize Davis's statements, but officials clearly stated that if Japan formally abolishes the Washington Treaty, the London Three-Power Talks have already ended. The only other option is for Japan to propose a naval limitation plan. (Reuters Telegram, 6th)

Pacific Aviation Route

San Francisco to Guangzhou

San Francisco has confirmed that the Pacific aviation route of the US airline is roughly as follows: From San Francisco to Guangzhou, stopping at Hawaii, Midway Island, Guam, and Manila. There will be one flight in each direction per week, with each trip taking 60 hours. Initially, only mail will be transported. After achieving success, passengers will be carried. Colonel Lindbergh will conduct further testing of flight conditions in the San Francisco area to determine whether it is suitable as the eastern terminal. The mileage is as follows:

San Francisco to Hawaii: 2,400 miles

Hawaii to Midway Island: 1,320 miles

Midway Island to Guam: 1,500 miles

Guam to Manila: 1,600 miles

Manila to Guangzhou: 700 miles

Total: 7,520 miles

(National Telegram, 6th)

Seiyukai Temporarily Softens, Japanese House of Representatives Continues to Meet

(Tokyo) At the budget general meeting, which was scheduled to open at 1:30 PM, Sunada Shigemasa, representing the Seiyukai, had learned of the government's sincerity. All the Seiyukai members welcomed Prime Minister Okada's response with applause. Because the Seiyukai expressed compromise, the atmosphere of dissolving the parliament has been completely swept away. (Dentsu Telegram, 7th)

(Tokyo) After the budget general meeting ended this afternoon, the government convened an extraordinary cabinet meeting, deciding to extend the parliamentary session by two days, because the crisis of dissolving the parliament has passed. (Japan United Telegram, 7th)

Seiyukai President Suzuki Decides on Compromise Measures

All-Night Meeting with Two Elders

Conditionally Approves Budget

(Tokyo) The Seiyukai's attitude towards the government budget could not be decided because there were hard-line and soft-line factions within the party. Therefore, it appointed President Suzuki to decide the verdict. On the evening of the 6th, Suzuki invited the two elders, Kuhara and Yamamoto, to his residence to negotiate until 2:00 AM the next morning. As a result of the three-person meeting, it was decided that the Seiyukai's attitude would be determined after confirming whether the government had sincerity at the budget general meeting. In other words, Prime Minister Okada's words alone could not understand the government's true intentions. However, the Seiyukai was afraid that submitting a separate resolution would cause serious political consequences, and this had to be avoided. Therefore, if the government showed sincerity at the budget general meeting on the 7th, respecting the Seiyukai's dignity, it could approve the government budget in view of the urgent implementation of the disaster budget, but this budget had to be subject to the conditions desired by the Seiyukai.

Since the Seiyukai president made a decision to approve the government budget, the talk of dissolving the parliament was slightly eased. However, the content of the conditions attached and the results of the budget general meeting still have the possibility of causing various problems. The future is still not optimistic. (Japan United Telegram, 7th)

(Tokyo) Nakamura Uemon, the chief secretary of the Seiyukai, was dissatisfied with the Seiyukai's attitude and submitted a party withdrawal letter to the Seiyukai headquarters on the 7th, and also submitted a resignation letter as a member of parliament to the parliament.

Kanai Masao and Kaneko Yosao, also of the Seiyukai, were dissatisfied with the party headquarters and declared their withdrawal from the Seiyukai on the 7th regarding the government's budget. (Japan United Telegram, 7th)

Continued Opening of the House of Representatives in Japan to Pass the Budget

Crisis of Dissolution Completely Eliminated

(Tokyo) Today, the Budget Committee convened at 1:30 PM in a tense atmosphere. Suzuki, President of the Seiyukai party, also attended as an observer. First, Chairman Shimada spoke, saying that Prime Minister Okada's responses at yesterday's meeting and the Seiyukai's deliberations to decide its stance had unfortunately delayed the start of the meeting. Seiyukai member To-bu-kun and other committee members requested the Chairman to inquire about the government's opinion. The Chairman, in deference to the members' wishes, asked the government: Prime Minister, in your response yesterday, you used phrases such as "willing to consider." Is that meant to convey willingness to consider the content of each Diet member's questions, or to consider the opinions of Diet members and the general public regarding the budget proposal? Please clarify.

Prime Minister Okada replied, "The government has absolutely no intention of disregarding public opinion and implementing politics. We will sincerely implement politics in the future, taking into consideration necessary facilities based on actual circumstances. If necessary in the future, we will consider necessary facilities. The government considers public opinion and implements politics. This is parliamentary politics."

Chairman Shimada asked, "Does the government intend to increase the disaster budget?"

Prime Minister Okada replied, "Beyond the current budget proposal, there is no intention to propose additional budget plans."

Chairman Shimada inquired whether any members of the Seiyukai party had comments to express. Okuchi Kiroku spoke, saying that the government's sincerity could be understood. According to the government's statement, the disaster budget was meticulously compiled, but upon actual observation of the situation, it is extremely inadequate.

Okuchi then described the plight of disaster-stricken areas, continuing, "How to rescue disaster areas is not only a problem that political parties should consider, but it is the opinion of the whole country. Since the Prime Minister has said that he will consider the overall will of the people and implement constitutional politics, we believe that the government is sincere. Therefore, we hope to immediately stop each person's questioning and begin discussing the motion proposed by the Seiyukai."

Prime Minister Okada said, "My statements will be reviewed in the minutes, and corrections may be made."

At this time, the assembly hall became noisy. Chairman Shimada said, "If the Prime Minister corrects his statement, we will have to temporarily suspend deliberations."

Prime Minister Okada replied, "The Chairman's interpretation seems to be a misunderstanding. Please continue deliberations."

Okuchi Kiroku then stood up and said, "I also believe that the Prime Minister's interpretation is the same as the Chairman's, so I have put forward a motion."

Chairman Shimada then declared a vote on Okuchi's motion, and the result was that it was adopted. The crisis of dissolving the Diet was thus eliminated. Thereafter, discussion began, the government's budget proposal was passed, and the meeting adjourned at 2:30 PM. (Jiji Press, 7th)

Center of Parliament Shifts to the House of Peers

Closing Ceremony to be Held on the 10th

(Tokyo) The House of Peers, having received the budget proposal from the House of Representatives on the evening of the 7th, convened a plenary session at 7:30 PM. First, Finance Minister Takahashi explained the disaster budget proposal, which was then entrusted to a committee. The meeting adjourned around 8:00 PM, and it was decided to convene the Budget Committee from 10:00 AM on the 8th to conduct discussions. (Jiji Press, 7th)

(Tokyo) The disaster budget proposal was passed by the Budget Committee of the House of Representatives on the afternoon of the 7th. Next, it will be approved by the plenary session and then submitted to the House of Peers. This extraordinary session of the Diet will be extended for two more days and is expected to conclude. On the morning of the 7th, due to Seiyukai President Suzuki's sudden unexpectedly firm stance, the government's attitude also hardened, and the possibility of dissolution became very strong. However, the crisis of dissolution has now been avoided. The Seiyukai and the government have reached a satisfactory resolution, so the center of the Diet has now shifted to the House of Peers. After concluding deliberations on the 8th and 9th, the closing ceremony is expected to be held on the 10th. (Jiji Press, 7th)

Page 8

European Crisis Turns Milder

Saar Plebiscite Problem Partially Resolved

Russia and France Deny Signing a Mutual Defense Pact

(Geneva) There are two new developments in the European situation today that are easing the crisis. The difficult problem of the Saarland residents' plebiscite on whether to belong to Germany, France, or maintain the status quo has been partially resolved. Germany has accepted the Saar Commission's proposal to send international police to maintain order in the Saar. Germany and France had each threatened residents and those who voted against them with retaliation, accusing each other. Now, according to an agreement, British, Italian, and other European countries will send troops to the Saar within a week. In addition, French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov have signed a treaty allowing France and Russia not to enter into any agreement that would hinder the Eastern Locarno Pact. Both representatives denied that there had been any alliance between France and Russia before and solemnly stated that this was the first treaty in which France and Russia adopted the same foreign policy. Recently, there was a saying in the French House of Representatives that France and Russia had already signed a military alliance treaty, saying that if Germany attacked France, Russia would help France attack Germany. Today, the statements of the French and Russian representatives have incidentally denied this statement. (Kokumin News Agency, 7th)

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Laval has signed an agreement with Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov stipulating that France and Russia shall not enter into non-aggression treaties with other countries without each other's consent, and especially shall not enter into any agreement that could affect the Eastern European Pact during the negotiations of the Eastern European Locarno Pact. (Kokumin News Agency, 7th)

Saar Problem Comes to an End, League of Nations Begins Discussion of South-Hungarian Case

French Foreign Minister Laval Acts as Mediator

Southern Representative's Speech is Surprisingly Moderate

(Geneva) Now that the Saar problem has come to an end, the eyes of the general public have now turned to Yugoslavia's application. From today, all parties have already begun to seek a fair way to resolve the dispute between South and Hungary. French Foreign Minister Laval continues to mediate, and he expressed optimism tonight. (Havas, 6th)

(Geneva) Today, the Council of the League of Nations convened a meeting to address Yugoslavia's accusation that Hungary was harboring accomplices in the Marseilles assassination. The speech given by South Foreign Minister Ivtić was moderate and unexpected. Mr. Ivtić only cited the events and the behavior of Hungarian officials. (Reuters, 7th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council, originally scheduled to meet this morning to discuss Yugoslavia's application regarding the political responsibility for the Marseilles assassination incident, has been postponed to 3 PM this afternoon. Hungarian Foreign Minister Kanya arrived in Geneva last night and held talks with representatives of major countries. As for the presentation of the South Foreign Minister Yevdić at the Council meeting this afternoon, he will explain that Yugoslavia's application is not a political lawsuit between Yugoslavia and Hungary, but is necessary to restore faith in the inherent order. Yevdić will also list various evidences of Hungary's responsibility for terrorist acts and demand that the League of Nations fulfill its duty to safeguard peace. Next, Czech Foreign Minister Beneš and Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu will present the opinions of the Little Entente countries. Then, the Hungarian representative Eckhardt will present Hungary's response. It is reported that Hungary, after the gentle persuasion of Britain and Italy, has decided to postpone the publication of its reply to Yugoslavia's application until tomorrow. (Havas, 7th)

Southern Country Expels Hungarian Overseas Chinese, Hungarian Government Protests

Two Thousand Refugees Wander at the Border with Nowhere to Go

Penniless, the Old and Weak Wailing, the Scene is Tragic

The Hungarian overseas Chinese expelled from South Ge-te have gathered in the border town of Ge-te in the past two days, and their total number has reached 1,308 men, women, and children. The scene this morning was unbearable. These drifters are temporarily residing in schools and hospitals to wait for transportation elsewhere. These people are thinly clothed, penniless, and carry only scattered furniture. Many are weak old men who have lived in the South for many years. There is a 14-year-old child with a broken leg, crying loudly to find his parents who were lost in the chaos. The remaining border stations are also full of helpless refugees waiting for the Hungarian government to transport them elsewhere by train. The South authorities have cut off the supply of vehicles. The Hungarian government has protested to the South government and asked European powers to pay attention to this matter. According to the refugees, the South military along the border has been transferred inland because these people are eager to attack Hungarian territory.

The Hungarian capital recently reported by the Hungarian Telegraphic Correspondence that a large number of Hungarians are being expelled by Yugoslavia and have arrived at the border. So far, Si-shi-te City has received 1,184 people, and Beike-shi City has received 214 people. (Havas, 7th)

Southern Country Government Defends Itself

Saying it Wants to Relieve Domestic Unemployment

Concentrates Troops on the Border, Denies Allegations

According to a Reuters reporter in Belgrade, the South National Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued an article stating that the expulsion of Hungarian overseas Chinese is reasonable and lawful. The South government, due to the serious problem of domestic unemployment, coupled with Hungary's attitude in Geneva and the Hungarian authorities' cancellation of the passports of hundreds of South nationals residing in Hungary, has decided not to renew the passports of 27,000 Hungarians working in the South territory. It also stated that this action has not caused any particular difficulty. (Reuters, 7th)

It is rumored from the Yugoslav capital that Yugoslav troops are concentrating on the Hungarian border. The Yava-la News Agency here officially denies this statement, saying that not only are Yugoslav troops not concentrating on the Hungarian border, but the Yugoslav troops originally stationed on the border have been reduced by 50% due to Christmas holidays. (Havas, 7th)

According to Hungarian sources in Ge-te Town, the South military stationed on the border is now crossing into Hungarian territory in an attempt to incite an incident. According to the Little Entente Treaty, if there is evidence that Hungary has committed an act of aggression, France will assist the South. According to Hungarian opinion, the South is now planning to create this situation. (Reuters, 7th)

International Police Force Enters the Saar, Germany's Reply Expresses Approval

Organized by Britain, Italy, Belgium, Switzerland, the Netherlands, etc.

The Number is at Most Two Thousand, Excluding Russia and Czechoslovakia

(Geneva) Regarding the dispatch of an international army to the Saar region to maintain law and order during the plebiscite, the German government submitted a reply to A-le-ya-xi, chairman of the Saar problem trio committee, at 6 p.m. tonight, stating, "When the League of Nations Council held a meeting yesterday, the German government has read the declaration issued by the representatives of various countries regarding the maintenance of law and order in the Saar region during the plebiscite. In the opinion of the German government, the security of the Saar does not necessarily have to be maintained by foreign troops, but if the Council of the League of Nations decides to send a small international army composed of neutral countries to the Saar, the German government also expresses its agreement." People here generally say that the German reply has brought the international stage of the Saar problem to an end. (Meaning that what remains is only the plebiscite, which is an internal problem of the Saar). The Council of the League of Nations may hold a meeting tomorrow morning to file the compromise on the issue of maintaining Saar's security. The establishment of this compromise is due to the proposal of French Foreign Minister Laval. Several British and Italian military officers will arrive here tomorrow to liaise with the agencies under the Council to organize the international army. (Havas, 6th)

(London) According to Geneva sources, although the German letter approved the dispatch of neutral international troops to the Saar, it believed that the current situation in the Saar did not require the use of foreign troops. When the German Consul in Geneva handed over this letter, he told the Secretary-General of the League of Nations that Germany had received guarantees from the governments of Britain and Italy. The so-called guarantees probably refer to Germany's concerns about the use of Russian troops, Czech troops, and the stationing of foreign troops in the Saar. According to reliable sources, Soviet Russia and Czechoslovakia have not requested to participate.

According to public opinion, an international police force of 1,500 to 2,000 people will be sufficient, and the members of this police force will be from Britain, Belgium, and Italy, because these three countries are all signatories to the Security Convention in the area. It is heard that the Netherlands has been invited and is expected to agree. In any case, this matter depends on the Saar Management Committee, and it is believed that the Committee will immediately start the organization plan of the international police force for the general assembly of citizens. (Reuters, 6th)

(Geneva) People in the League of Nations believe that Sweden and the Netherlands may be invited to send a small team to join the UK and Italy to form an international army to enter the Saar to maintain order. These people also believe that the UK will send two battalions of infantry, and Italy will send two battalions of cavalry. (Havas, 6th)

The report of the Saar Tripartite Committee has now been passed by the entire Council of the League of Nations, and both France and Germany have approved of Britain's cooperation in maintaining order during the plebiscite, and both have stated that they do not want to participate in the international army, so one thing that needs to be resolved later is the concrete methods that should be adopted during and after the plebiscite to maintain order.

The British Knox, chairman of the Saar Management Committee, told the Council of the League of Nations yesterday that his current limited police force cannot guarantee that he can maintain order in an emergency. If an international army is stationed in the territory in advance, the Management Committee feels that order can be maintained, and the voting conference and the difficult times thereafter will definitely pass safely.

French Foreign Minister Laval told the Council of the League of Nations that the Saar procedure is not French, nor German, but for the League of Nations, so he said that the Council must be responsible for deciding what can maintain order. (Reuters, 6th)

Simon Reports to the House of Commons

Praises the Spirit of Cooperation of the Countries Concerned

Dispatching Troops Together is Beneficial to the UK

(London) British Foreign Minister Simon announced this afternoon in a crowded House of Commons that good news had been received that the problem of dispatching police to maintain order during the Saar plebiscite had been resolved in principle. Simon spoke for a long time, praising the work of the tripartite committee in agreeing on recommendations that had been accepted by both France and Germany, and praising the spirit of cooperation shown by countries with immediate relations with the future of the Saar. Simon said that the British government has always held the view that if disturbances occur during or after the Saar plebiscite, it is not appropriate for France to be the only country to provide external assistance. A few days ago, British representative Eden had offered cooperation. I can now happily tell you that I have received a reply from the German government, which states that the German government believes that it is very beneficial to have international troops stationed in the Saar before and after the Saar plebiscite. It also said that the German government approves of the condition that France and Germany do not join this army. I can also announce that Italy is also willing to undertake cooperation under the same conditions as the British government. The British government is currently in contact with several countries. French Foreign Minister Laval immediately expressed his agreement. I hope that everything I have said will satisfy the House of Commons, because the British government is handling this matter with due consideration for British interests, and also has the firmest intention to ensure the orderly conduct of the plebiscite under the authority of the League of Nations. Maintaining its order is the responsibility of the League of Nations, and the United Kingdom, under the guidance of the League of Nations, should also fulfill its proper obligations. After Simon's speech, everyone cheered, and Labor Party leader Lansbury and Liberal Party member Foote also congratulated the Foreign Minister. (Reuters, 7th)

US Replies to the League of Nations Regarding the Chaco Dispute Mediation

Refuses to Participate in the Work of the Advisory Committee

Paraguayan Troops Continuously Occupy Bolivian Fortresses, the Momentum is Like a Broken Bamboo

(Washington) The League of Nations' Advisory Committee for the mediation of the Chaco dispute had also invited the United States government to participate in cooperation. The United States government has recently replied, saying that the United States will not participate in the work of the Advisory Committee for the Chaco dispute, because the United States is not a member of the League of Nations, but the United States will send a Consul General stationed in Geneva to continue to have formal contact with the Advisory Committee and, when necessary, order him to notify the United States government at any time. On the contrary, the United States has accepted to participate in the Neutral Country Committee monitoring the ceasefire between Ba-Bo, and the arbitration meeting in the capital of Argentina. (Havas, 7th)

Asunción Today, it is expected here that the Paraguayan army will drive straight in and may soon invade the Bolivian mainland. In the past two days, the Paraguayan army has repeatedly captured five gun emplacements, and two more are about to be captured. The fall of the five gun emplacements was like cutting rotten weeds. It is said that the Dao-bie-ni gun emplacement and the Ke-ke-lun gun emplacement have also been broken, but this news has not yet been confirmed. If this is the case, Vila-Montes may fall within 48 hours, and a major invasion of Bolivian territory will occur. The Bolivian army has completely lost its fighting spirit and has repeatedly abandoned its positions, leaving weapons and firearms everywhere. The Paraguayan army, under the command of General Ais-tai-ge-la, has advanced 60 miles and now surrounds the strategic location of Vila-Montes on three sides, which is the gateway to the Chaco oil area. Newspapers in Asunción reported that the Bolivian army, due to political turmoil, lacks the support of the government and also lacks weapons, and is on the verge of rebellion. The Paraguayan army will launch a general attack on Vila-Montes at any time and will surely win, because it is believed here that the Bolivian army has been surrounded on three sides, lacks both food and weapons, and can only support it for at most one or two days. (Kokumin News Agency, 6th)

French Foreign Minister's Tour of Italy May Not Be Far Away

(Geneva) The negotiations between the French and Italian representatives in Geneva have made considerable progress. It is expected that French Foreign Minister Laval may visit Rome soon. Former French Foreign Minister Barthou had a plan to visit Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Italy, but it was suspended due to Barthou being assassinated. Afterwards, Laval and Mussolini looked forward to meeting each other, and it was quite eager. At present, the spirit of compromise between the French and Italian representatives in Geneva is indeed a prelude to this meeting. (Havas, 7th)

Abyssinian People Suddenly Attack Italian Sentry Camp

Italy Urgently Mobilizes Reinforcements to Repel Them

Abandoned Bullets Reach a Distance of Ten Miles

Rome A large team of Abyssinian people, carrying machine guns, rifles, and a cannon, suddenly attacked an Italian military sentry camp in the Italian Somali-Lun district of Wei-lu-ya-lu-ya-er today. The Italian army urgently mobilized reinforcements to fight and repelled the Abyssinian people. The abandoned bullets were scattered ten miles away. In mid-November, the Abyssinian people attacked the Italian Consulate in Gong-da, killing one guard and wounding two others. Italy then lodged a serious protest, and the Abyssinian authorities had admitted the claim for compensation. (Reuters, 7th)

Siamese Government Representative Arrives in Britain to Plead for the King to Return Home

(London) The Siamese government representative country has now arrived here to request the King of Siam to cancel his intention to abdicate. The King of Siam will hold his first meeting with the representatives at the beginning of next week, but according to the people around the King, the King's intention to abdicate is very firm and he will not return to the throne. Moreover, the King intends to live in Britain for a long time. (Kokumin News Agency, 7th)

(Paris) The Siamese government representative who was ordered to end the dispute between the King of Siam and the Parliament is on his way to Britain and passed through here today. He is the Speaker of the People's House of the Siamese Parliament, the Secretary-General of the Senate, and the Secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. According to them, the people of Siam are eager for the King to cancel his abdication and return to the country to govern. (Reuters, 6th)

Bangkok The Siamese government has ordered that the people must not be allowed to know the news of the King of Siam's abdication and has implemented extremely strict inspection orders. No newspaper dares to violate this order, but the Malay newspaper took this opportunity to publish Siamese news and sell it here, and buyers scrambled for it. (Reuters communication, November 24th)

Göring Declares Irrelevance in the German Parliament Arson Case

The French Newspaper's Report is Completely Fabricated

(Berlin) On Tuesday, the Paris Daily published an alarming document proving that the burning of the German Parliament was tacitly approved by Propaganda Minister Goebbels and Prussian Prime Minister Göring. Today, Göring's secretary declared that Ernst's statement was completely false. General Göring does not want to defend this matter, because there are many rumors fabricated by enemies outside, and it is really impossible to defend against them. According to the document, it was personally signed by Ernst, the leader of the Berlin Stormtroopers who was shot during the National Socialist purge movement in June of this year, proving that the fire in the Parliament was tacitly approved by the Second Ge, hoping to destroy the credibility of the Communist Party and consolidate the power of the National Socialist Party. (Reuters, 6th)

All-India Congress Opposes the Indian Constitutional Reform Draft

Demanding Complete Independence and Autonomy

After two days of secret discussions, the All-India National Congress in Mumbai has passed a resolution, reiterating that India should be completely autonomous. As for the draft Indian Constitution proposed by Britain, it will be resolutely rejected. However, the resolution has not yet expressed its position on the issue of boycotting Britain. (Havas, 6th)

Tarzan of the Apes Author Divorces

Thirty-Four Years of Marriage End in Separation

American La Wei-gesi, known to the world as the author of "Tarzan of the Apes", Bai Luosi, divorced his wife here today, after 34 years of marriage. The reason is that his wife's personality is unusually cruel. She gave birth to three sons in the thirty-six years of marriage. In his youth, Bai was a soldier, policeman, gold miner, and shop assistant, and later engaged in writing. In 1914, the book "Tarzan of the Apes" was published and became popular around the world, and his reputation was greatly enhanced. (Reuters, 6th)

Page 9

US Senator Announces Arms Transferred from Europe to China

(Washington) Senator Clark made a statement today at the Senate Arms Investigation Committee, saying that there is really no need for war to occur in the world unless it is for the benefit of arms manufacturers. In 1929, a certain company disregarded the government's ban on the transportation of arms to China and shipped a batch of gunpowder to the Netherlands, and then transshipped it to China. The company knew that this batch of gunpowder would eventually be transported to China, but because the government had no right to prohibit transportation to the Netherlands, it rashly started shipping in order to be opportunistic. In addition, Clark also mentioned the issue of the United States selling 20 million bullets to Bolivia between 1933 and 1934, saying that Paraguay only purchased 10,000 bullets from the United States, and the rest was supplied by manufacturers in Britain and Germany. At this point, Clark then presented a letter from a certain US arms company to its representative in Chile, which read: "Regarding the issue of arms embargo, we have contacted important official figures, and we can fully justify and eliminate this unconscious move, etc." (Havas, 6th)

Soviet Russia Opens Central Committee Plenary Session

Two Hundred People Exiled to Siberia

(Moscow) According to semi-official news, the Central Committee of the Communist Party will hold a plenary session at the end of next week, chaired by Stalin, to deal with internal affairs and select a successor to Kirov. According to another message, 200 relatives of the 71 people executed in Moscow and Leningrad yesterday have been exiled to Siberia for a period of three to ten years, and the property of the exiles has also been confiscated. (Kokumin News Agency, 7th)

German Judicial Unification

(Berlin) According to government orders, all judicial departments in the country (formerly states) except Prussia have been abolished. Previously, the national judicial system had been unified, and its judicial power was entirely in the hands of the central government. In the past, the legal systems of various German states were different, and each had its own judicial department. (Havas, 6th)

The Chinese New School of Painting's Show of English Brilliance Opens to the Public

(London) One hundred fifty to two hundred pieces of Chinese new school paintings, which had been exhibited in Rome, Milan, Berlin, and Paris with the assistance of the respective governments and greatly admired by the audience, have now been shipped from Europe to the Chinese Legation here. Among them are works by fifteen Chinese famous painters such as Liu Haisu. The French government recently purchased one of Liu's paintings. Recently, after the premiere of Mr. Xiong's adaptation of the Chinese ancient drama "Wang Baochuan" at the Little Theatre, it aroused the interest of the British people in Chinese art. Therefore, this painting exhibition is guaranteed to achieve beautiful results. Bao Yueqing is About to Go to the Temple for a Trip

International Commercial Telegram

Special Commercial News Telegram from Reuters on December 7th –

Gold and Silver

English Gold: The London gold price today was quoted at 140 shillings and 3.5 pence, a decrease of 3.5 pence.

English Silver: The London silver price today decreased by 0.1875. The spot price is 24.6875 pence, and the futures price is 24.8125 pence. China sold, and purchases were not strong when prices fell. The market situation at the close was stable.

American Silver: Although the Mount Lyell silver futures market failed to maintain its initial upward momentum, it still rose by about 60 pounds.

Indian Silver: The Bombay silver market was quiet today. The spot closing price was 67 rupees and 4 annas, a decrease of 4 annas.

Exchange Rates

English-American: The London foreign exchange market was trading well this morning. The authorities did not use the Exchange Equalisation Account. The opening exchange rate for English pounds against US dollars was 4 dollars, 90 cents and 5,9375, which is lower than the closing exchange rate between the US and England yesterday by 0.0625.

Before noon, the British pound showed slight fatigue. The latest price was 4 dollars and 90 cents and 1875, which is 0.75 lower than the opening. Also, one US dollar equals 4 shillings and 0.0466 English gold.

English-French: The opening remained unchanged at 75 francs and 28 centimes, a decrease of 19 pounds, down to 75 francs and 09. The most recent price was 75 francs and 15 centimes, up 6 pounds.

US-English: The New York foreign exchange market. The British pound is still weak. The opening exchange rate for English pounds against US dollars was 4 dollars and 90 cents and 5,25, which is 0.75 lower than yesterday, and there were no changes afterwards.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: Observers of the cotton market say that the cotton market will be very sluggish in the near future. Although the basic prices are stable and there is hope for the continuation of the Penhaid case, the cotton price will not fall sharply. However, export demand has not yet recovered, so the cotton price will not rise either. Today, the cotton market opened up 2 pounds, but soon fell to yesterday's closing price, with mixed ups and downs. Transactions were not high. Liverpool and its counterparts bought in at the opening.

Indian Cotton: In the Bombay cotton market, market operators and speculators are buying futures. The price of white cotton for the April-May period is 226 rupees and 75, up one rupee.

English Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was looser this morning. At 1:00 PM, the price for the May contract was 6.69, three pounds lower than yesterday's close.

English Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was firmer today. At 1:00 PM, the price for the May contract was 5 shillings and 5.375 pence, up 0.375. The US wheat market opened strong today, with prices up by more than one cent. This is due to bad weather news from Argentina and very cold weather in the US grain, which will extend elsewhere. It is heard that Australia is now selling wheat to the East. The movements in our wheat market can be seen as exciting.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market is calm. The成交prices for the April-June period at noon were 6.625 pence, the same as yesterday's price.

New York: The New York rubber market opened down 5 pounds. Since then, the ups and downs are mixed, and the transactions are very small.

Securities

New York: Before the opening of the New York stock market, the factors favorable to the market situation are (1) Although the stock market is now consolidating its position, there is no sign of loss of confidence. (2) The demand of investors and speculators is expected to remain unsatisfied. (3) Cooperation between the business community and the government is expected to eventually revive commerce. (4) The amount of bank bill exchanges this week has increased compared to the previous week. The unfavorable factors for the market situation are that there is a wait-and-see and suspicious atmosphere in the market regarding railway stocks, fearing that the railway freight volume report will not be satisfactory. The stock market may therefore suffer setbacks. The stock market opened this morning, with flat trading and mixed prices. The ups and downs are limited to single-digit numbers, and the sentiment is still good, but the market price does not seem to fluctuate much at one time. The market prices are as follows:

The Shandong Department of Finance Promulgates Measures to Restrict the Exit of Silver Currency

(Jinan) The Department of Finance promulgated four measures to restrict the exit of silver currency: The limit within the province is 300 yuan, and the limit for leaving the province is 20 yuan.
