The Full Text of Guo Taiqi's Speech at the 15th Session of the League of Nations Assembly

Declaring China's Position on the Northeast Issue

On September 14th of this year, when the 15th session of the League of Nations Assembly in Geneva was held, Guo Taiqi, the Chief Representative of our country and Minister to the United Kingdom, stood up and delivered a speech after the Secretary-General Dr. Avenol (Representative of Czechoslovakia) presented the annual report, claiming to speak in the capacity of the League of Nations Far East Rapporteur. He detailed the situation caused by Japan's armed occupation of Manchuria and several provinces in the Far East of China, and at the same time announced China's stance and attitude in abiding by the League of Nations' resolution on the Lytton Report. A summary of his speech was published in this newspaper on September 15th. Yesterday, the Shanghai China Press published the full text, which we have translated as follows:

Minister Guo said, "It is not merely a formality to extend congratulations to the Secretary-General for presenting his first annual report since taking office. He elaborated on the fate of the League of Nations in its most critical year. He sees the League of Nations regaining its prestige and emerging from this year. The despair that recently led one or two countries to abandon the League of Nations in search of solutions has now made the whole world realize that the soundness and stability of international cooperation can only lie within the framework of the League of Nations. China supports this renewed global sentiment without any reservations. The Chinese delegation, in the name of one-fifth of the world's people, in the name of one of the governments with the longest history of national administration, and in the name of the largest force in Asia, welcomes the clear signs of the restored power of the League of Nations. However, China does not hold excessive optimism, just as it despises excessive pessimism. In his opening address to the Assembly, Mr. Avenol spoke eloquently about the current situation in the world. I cannot hope to match Mr. Avenol's extensive knowledge and clear insights, but I must strive to compete with his pragmatic realism and focus on the points in the world situation that are most relevant to the Far East and that the Chinese government believes are most harmful to the future of world peace. Mr. Avenol's analysis of the situation draws attention to the hidden dangers of peace in the Far East. He said, "The current situation between China and Japan and the existing tensions between China and Russia are both particularly significant, and no one can deny this." My speech is not based on the position of one party in a dispute, but rather on the position of the League of Nations Far East Rapporteur, who must ask you for tolerance, and is based on the report accepted by all loyal members of the League of Nations regarding the nature and responsibility of the current tensions in the Far East. This report places the responsibility of paying close attention to the development of events in the Far East on the Assembly. The reason why I make these remarks is to assist us gathered here in fulfilling this responsibility. There are three main points that I would like to bring to the attention of the Assembly:

The first point is that the entire case is still open. The puppet installed by a certain foreign power in several provinces of Northeast China now calls himself emperor. This has not changed the nature of the armed occupation that violates the League of Nations Covenant. China only endures when it must endure. The League of Nations as a whole has passed its final judgment on this occupation. The League of Nations is still bound by its judgment. A year ago, when the Assembly opened its annual meeting, the Chinese representative stated that the Chinese government regards the situation in the four provinces as a fixed violation of the treaties, on which the security, disarmament, and peace of the world at large will depend. The Chinese government is determined to steadfastly maintain all its rights and demands and will never recognize or acquiesce to the fact created by the constitution. This kind of fact created by illegal means will only remain when China is unable to do so in terms of national strength or the rest of the League of Nations is unable to uphold the dignity of the treaties politically.

Our country holds this attitude because we believe that we have not only exhausted our helpless power to maintain the integrity of China's territory and political independence to resist Japanese aggression, but China's move is also aimed at resisting the attempt to transform the League of Nations Covenant into a mere scrap of paper. Subsequently, the Assembly adopted its unanimous report of February 24, 1933. China has strictly abided by the obligations contained in the various articles of the resolution in the report and fully expects the recommendations in the report to be implemented quickly without delay. In particular, with regard to the issue of non-recognition of the puppet state, China's attitude is firm and unwavering. China not only upholds this principle of non-recognition itself, but also believes that all countries in the League of Nations and other countries that have agreed to this principle have a responsibility to uphold it. Now, a certain distant country has formally recognized the illegal organization in Northeast China, although it is ambiguous. In fact, that country itself rarely has any direct contact with East Asian affairs. The circumstances of the recognition, as I have said, are still ambiguous. From China's standpoint as a member of the League of Nations, it regards this action as violating the League of Nations Covenant and as an event that the League of Nations should study and punish. Moreover, it believes that no other member state of the League of Nations will regard international justice with the same behavior, violating the provisions of the resolution in the unanimous report and its own solemn obligations listed in the report. This solitary incident is not worth mentioning, but in theory, it is very serious. The judgment of the League of Nations has maintained its inviolability to deal with actions that take the opportunity to induce destruction. This is indeed a great achievement. We Chinese are not unaware that some people are making efforts everywhere to stir up some ambiguity and hesitation in maintaining this inviolability. If they recently made unremitting attempts to threaten those who do not recognize the illegal system in that part of China with economic rectification and to make it difficult for their consuls stationed in Manchuria, to intimidate the countries bound by the Assembly's report, and to induce them to submit with special economic interests. Regarding this section, there are things that can be traced back. The Assembly's report not only obligates countries to recognize it in fact or in law, but also must not take any action that would facilitate the maintenance of the current illegal system. When the Advisory Committee of the Assembly interpreted this obligation, it stated that the governments of various countries cannot protect those who seek concessions from the custodians of the illegal system, because this illegal system disposes of China's state-owned property and commits the crime of high treason under international law. All claims based on this kind of opportunistic behavior can obviously not be recognized by China or any country bound by the Assembly's report. The Chinese government may file a lawsuit in any court of a country bound by the Assembly's report against those who enjoy concessions granted by the authorities in Manchuria who are destroying treaties, demanding compensation for losses. This is also an obvious fact.

The second point I would like to inform you is that the League of Nations has a continuous responsibility for this matter. This responsibility gradually increases with the increasing tension in the Far East situation and the growing hidden dangers to peace in the Far East. The refusal of any country to participate in the Geneva Conference does not affect this, because the League of Nations Covenant states that no country can terminate its membership in the League of Nations until its international obligations are fully fulfilled. This is not an unimportant provision, but a crucial and fundamental obligation. If any country can arbitrarily violate the Covenant and escape the pear of its withdrawal from the League of Nations, then the League of Nations as an instrument of peace will become a broken reed. The Assembly has solemnly declared that today's armed occupation of Manchuria is an act that violates the League of Nations Covenant, the Nine-Power Treaty, and the Kellogg-Briand Pact. The Assembly, as the defender of the League of Nations' honor, is responsible for drawing a clear conclusion on the basis of its own declaration and the provisions of the Covenant that I have just cited.

The third point I would like to ask you to pay attention to is the most important point, that is, the consequences of continuing to carry out treaty-breaking aggression in the Far East have now affected the whole world. The Assembly's report, which condemned this aggression and determined its responsibility, also stated that the continuation of the current system in Manchuria is incompatible with the maintenance of peace in the Far East. The Lytton Report also stated that any system that does not have the willing cooperation of the people of Manchuria cannot restore order and prosperity in that part of China, and that the people of Manchuria are now firmly opposed to the foreign military dictatorship that should be regarded as created by fraud and aggression. The facts have unfortunately proved how correct the Assembly's view of the situation created by the occupation of our northeastern provinces is. As of today, the situation has not improved at all and is even further away from what the League of Nations previously hoped for and decided on. In March of this year, the illegal organization actually declared itself an empire, and its puppet even usurped the title of emperor. Although this does not change the nature and status of the puppet state, the illegality of the case has reached a more dangerous degree. (To be continued)

Fierce Battle Between the Northeastern Anti-Japanese Volunteers and Japanese-Puppet Troops in Jidong

Japanese-Puppet Troops Organize a Joint Force to Attack

Anti-Japanese Volunteers Fight Fiercely in Their Respective Areas

Changchun Correspondence: Since the Japanese army forcibly occupied our Northeast, the people of our Northeast, although under great oppression, have never ceased their efforts to resist. Despite failures and sacrifices, their spirit has not been broken. Therefore, they press forward one after another, unyielding and indomitable. The situation this year is particularly intense. Although the network of roads built by the Japanese army is largely completed, allowing travel from morning to evening, the people of the Northeast are still fighting like trapped beasts in the midst of hardship, shattering the Japanese propaganda that "Manchukuo's public order has entered a safe period, and military operations have come to an end." This demonstrates the fighting spirit of our Chinese nation. Because of this, the Japanese army is restless day and night and considers the situation serious. They have taken large-scale mobilization actions to cope with it. In addition to the area along the Liaoning Eastern Border, where the Japanese Independent First Garrison Unit, in conjunction with puppet troops, is commanded by the Garrison Commander Miura and has begun attacking, recently, the Japanese Wakayama Division (Third Division), stationed in Harbin, has been the main force. It has drawn troops from the Tani Brigade of the Japanese Seventh Division stationed in Rehe, and the Shinohara and Kozhiba Regiments of the Sixteenth Division in Qiqihar, along with the entire First Army of the "Fengtian" Puppet Jing'an Guerrilla Force, to form a joint Japanese-puppet force. Corresponding to the Japanese-puppet troops stationed in the defense area, they have surrounded the area of activity of the Anti-Japanese Volunteers in the northeastern part of Jilin Province, allocated areas, and begun attacking. The Anti-Japanese Volunteers in various parts of northeastern Jilin Province, upon receiving the news, are all in high spirits, vowing to fight to the death with the Japanese-puppet troops. They have been in contact for several days. The deployment of the Japanese-puppet troops and their attacks on the Anti-Japanese Volunteers are recorded as follows:

(1) Binjiang Area: The Three-Kai and Yasui Regiments belonging to the Japanese Third Division are taking a large encirclement formation against the elite units of the Anti-Japanese Volunteers led by Yu Haiyun (Jiujiang) and Zhao Shangzhi, and fierce battles are taking place in areas such as Yangshan (15 kilometers east of Wuchang County on the Labin Line), Mao'er Mountain (along the Hasui Line), Heilong Palace (southeast of the Bin Line), Tongbin (Yanshou), and other areas.

(2) Ning'an Area: The Japanese army, with the Tani Brigade and its subordinate regiments of the Seventh Division stationed in Rehe as the main force, is attacking the various Anti-Japanese Volunteer units in the Ning'an area. It has already engaged in a fierce battle with the forces linked to Chen Dongshan's unit in the western part of the Aimin Ninth Battalion at Nanhu Tou (Jingpo Lake).

(3) Eastern Area: The Japanese army, drawing elite Saito, Yoshiki, and Minamikosuge Regiments (combined to form a brigade or more in strength) from the Third, Seventh, and Sixteenth Divisions, is dividing into three routes, each taking one side, to attack the powerful Anti-Japanese Volunteer force led by Kong Xianrong, which is located near the Russian border. Their strategic plan is to use a siege formation and adopt a joint army-air force threat tactic to suppress Kong's force. However, Kong's force is very strong, and they have a considerable source of arms and ammunition, so they should be able to sustain the fight for a long time.

(4) Northern Area: The Japanese army in Yilan, Fangzheng, Jiamusi, and other places, with the Tamura Regiment, Abunzuku Detachment, and Kozhiba Detachment (all battalion-level), organized a joint attack against the Anti-Japanese Volunteer force led by Xie Wendong. They have already engaged in fierce battles in Changfa Tun, Banjie He, Taiping Gou, and other places. Two Japanese Second Lieutenants, Kajio and Matsuda, have been killed.

It is found that the Anti-Japanese Volunteers are very active in the northeastern part of Jilin, and there are three reasons why the Japanese-puppet troops are difficult to deal with: (1) Being close to the border, it is easy for the Anti-Japanese Volunteers to replenish their guns and ammunition, and even if they run out of ammunition and are cut off from supplies, there is still a source; (2) The local people are deeply stimulated by the confiscation of guns and land, and they clearly know the brutal face of the Japanese, so they are determined to resist Japan and secretly help the Anti-Japanese armed forces; (3) The northeastern part of Jilin is close to mountainous areas, and most of the land is large-scale silty fields. In this kind of place, only the natives who are familiar with the situation can pass through unhindered with skillful techniques, so the Japanese regard it as a daunting task, and transportation by cars, etc., is even more impossible. With these three reasons, the Anti-Japanese Volunteers can wage a protracted war. (Northeast News Agency)

The Situation of Bandits in Sichuan and Hunan

Internal Division Has Already Begun Among the Sichuan Bandits

The Focus of Bandit Suppression Will Be in Sichuan in the Future

Hankou Correspondence: After Xu Xiangqian's bandit forces rampaged in northern Sichuan, bandit gangs in various places, feeling unable to survive under the pressure of the National Army, all thought about fleeing to Sichuan to join forces. In recent times, those who have abandoned their nests and fled westward, such as the Jiangxi bandits entering Hunan, and the bandits on the border of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Shanxi, are also plotting to enter Shaanxi, which is all evidence of this. The resurgence of the Sichuan bandits in Suixuan and the return of He Long and Xiao Ke to western Hunan also have a significant role in connecting with the westward fleeing of the Jiangxi bandits. The border area of Sichuan, Hunan, and Hubei will be the focus of future military operations to suppress bandits, and the area around Hankou is sufficient for control. As for the strength of the various bandit forces, Zhu Mao is rampaging with all his forces and is being surrounded and suppressed by the National Army on all sides, and their strength has become weak. The He and Xiao gangs are not the main force, and the Wu Huanxian gang has less than a thousand people, which is even less worth mentioning. Combining news from various sources: (1) Xu Xiangqian's gang occupies more than ten counties in northern Sichuan, such as Banan. Following the old tricks of the Jiangxi bandits, they established a puppet "Chinese Soviet Republic." Its highest military organ is the puppet "Northwest Revolutionary Military Commission," with Zhang Guotao as the puppet chairman. Under it are the puppet "Northwest Military Region Political Department," with Chen Changhao as the puppet director, the puppet "General Staff Department," with Ni Zhiliang as the puppet chief of staff, and the puppet "General Headquarters of the Northwest Military Region of the Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Army," with Xu Xiangqian as the puppet commander-in-chief and Wang Shulin as the puppet deputy commander-in-chief. Under it are five armies: the puppet Fourth Army, commanded by Wang Hongkun, commanding the Tenth, Eleventh, and Twelfth Divisions, with the Twelfth Division as the main force, being the most elite among the armies; the puppet Ninth Army, commanded by He Wei, commanding the Twenty-fifth, Twenty-sixth, and Twenty-seventh Divisions; the puppet Thirtieth Army, commanded by Yu Tianyun, commanding the Eighty-eighth, Eighty-ninth, and Ninetieth Divisions; the puppet Thirty-first Army, commanded by Sun Yuqing, commanding the Ninety-first, Ninety-second, and Ninety-third Divisions, all with average combat capabilities; and the puppet Thirty-third Army, commanded by Wang Weizhou, commanding the Ninety-seventh and Ninety-eighth Divisions, with the weakest strength. Although the bandits possess this huge force, the cadres from Hubei and Henan have died almost completely, and those who have been replenished are all Sichuanese, so they are still easy to pacify. According to a recent Sichuan telegram, it is said that Xu, realizing that it would be difficult to succeed due to the disunity within the bandit gang, secretly sent representatives to express their sincerity to the central government and requested that troops be sent to Shaanxi to provide cover so that they could lead their troops to return. However, the plan was leaked and they were secretly executed by Chen Changhao and Zhang Guotao. In order to stabilize the bandits, they still claimed to the outside world that Xu was responsible for military affairs, but in reality, Zhang was in command. Although the truth of the matter cannot be determined, internal strife among the bandits is indeed possible. The recent actions of the Sichuan bandits are that the right wing mainly defends, with many fortifications built on the north bank of the Ba River, and the left wing mainly attacks, plotting to once again rampage in Suixuan, attempting to spy on Kui Wan. The Sichuan army is currently taking strict precautions. After Liu Xiang returns to Sichuan after meeting with Chiang Kai-shek, he will order a general suppression. The various troops stationed in [illegible] have already obeyed the order to cooperate in the suppression. Once the Sichuan army launches an attack, they will join forces to advance and suppress. (2) The puppet First, Third, Fifth, Eighth, and Ninth Army Corps of the Jiangxi bandits, unable to gain a foothold in Jiangxi, entered Sichuan via Hunan. One force has crossed Quanyong, and another force is trapped on the Guibian, and fierce battles have been raging for days, with no less than 20,000 bandits killed or captured. (3) The He Long and Xiao Ke gangs, entrenched in western Hunan, number about several thousand people. They are currently surrounded in Dayong by the Hubei army, the Hunan army, [illegible] Chen Quzhen's various units, and are still fleeing downwards very rapidly. (4) The Wu Huanxian gang, rampaging on the border of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, has been defeated by [illegible] and other units. They have less than a thousand people. They merged the puppet Twenty-eighth Army into the puppet Twenty-fifth Army. The puppet Northeast Road and its subordinate two puppet guerrilla divisions were also completely merged, and they were reorganized into the Seventy-fourth and Seventy-fifth Divisions. Now they have been reduced to the Seventy-fifth Division. The puppet commander was formerly sent by the Jiangxi bandits, and Xu Haidong is the puppet deputy commander. Wu has retreated to become the puppet commander and political commissar of the Seventy-fifth Division. They are still continuing to flee westward, but they are no longer a cause for concern. (6th)

Guangdong Province Holds Winter Defense

Various Counties Formulate Winter Defense Measures for Implementation

Authorities Dispatch Personnel to Inspect Police Teams Throughout the Province

Guangzhou Correspondence: As winter defense is approaching, and the bandits on the border of Hunan, Guangxi, and Guangdong are currently being jointly encircled and suppressed, the public order in the interior of Guangdong Province is important. The authorities have instructed various pacification district offices to issue orders to their subordinate counties and cities to hold winter defense preparedness to prevent petty thieves and bandits from mixing in. The various counties, upon receiving the order, have formulated winter defense measures separately and are implementing them uniformly. The guard office of the headquarters, in order to inspect the guard teams of various counties, assess their performance, and inspect the situation of their deployment, has dispatched supervisory commissioners to inspect the districts in daytime. According to the terrain of the various counties in the province, it has been divided into sixteen supervisory areas for guard teams. One supervisory commissioner is assigned to each area to inspect the counties on a rotating basis. The supervisory commissioners are rotated every six months. The supervisory commissioners have been successively appointed, and the delineation of the supervisory areas is as follows: (First District) Nanhai, Sanshui, Huaxian, Qingyuan, Fogang, Conghua; (Second District) Panyu, Shunde, Baoan, Dongguan, Zengcheng, Longmen; (Third District) Zhongshan, Xinhui, Taishan, Chixi, Kaiping, Enping; (Fourth District) Huiyang, Heyuan, Boluo, Zijin, Haifeng, Lufeng; (Fifth District) Xinfeng, Lianping, Heping, Longchuan, Wuhua, Xingning; (Sixth District) Raoping, Dapu, Fengshun, Meixian, Pingyuan, Jiaoling; (Seventh District) Nanao, Chenghai, Chaoyang, Huilai, Puning, Jieyang, Chaoan; (Eighth District) Qujiang, Shixing, Nanxiong, Lechang, Renhua, Ruyuan, Wengyuan; (Ninth District) Yingde, Yangshan, Lianxian, Lianshan; (Tenth District) Sihui, Guangning, Heshan, Gaoyao, Gaoming, Xinxing; (Eleventh District) Yunfu, Deqing, Luoding, Yunan, Fengchuan, Kaijian; (Twelfth District) Yangjiang, Yangchun, Dianbai, Wuchuan, Maoming, Xinyi; (Thirteenth District) Huaxian, Lianjiang, Suixi, Haikang, Xuwen; (Fourteenth District) Hepu, Lingshan, Qinxian, Fangcheng; (Fifteenth District) Qiongshan, Chengmai, Lingao, Danxian, Changjiang, Ganen; (Sixteenth District) Wenchang, Anding, Qiongdong, Lehui, Wanning, Lingshui, Yaxian. (2nd)

Implementation of Feast Tax in Beiping

Over Two Thousand Yuan Collected in a Short Period

Beiping Correspondence: Since the abolition of miscellaneous levies in Beiping, the market has shown a slight recovery, but government expenses and all construction costs have become tight. The municipal government has levied a feast tax in an attempt to make up for this. The intention is to raise funds while curbing extravagance and waste. The tax has been in effect for twenty days, and the amount collected has reached a huge sum of over two thousand yuan. The citizens' monthly expenses for socializing and entertainment, as evidenced by this, are quite shocking. According to Wang Yinhuai, the director in charge of this tax, the process and current situation of the tax are briefly described as follows: "The feast tax in this city is an innovation, so since our office has undertaken the special levy, we have taken many things into consideration. The funds advanced for the undertaking are not small, and the difficulty of promotion is still felt to be thorny. When the municipal government promulgated the regulations, the guild of restaurant operators initially requested exemption, and then refused to collect on their behalf. It was not until November 8 that the implementation was slightly in order. Furthermore, due to sending personnel to distribute joint orders and various procedures, it was not until November 10 that it was truly the first day of collection. In the first ten days of November, the collection had not yet begun, so there was no income. In the middle ten days, a total of cash and arrears were collected, deducting 5% of the cost for collection on behalf, the actual donation of foreign money amounted to two thousand six hundred thirty-six yuan, three corners and six cents, which is the result of the total collection of each household up to today." (6th)

Impersonating Inspectors to Rob Under the Pretext of Inspecting Soil in Songjiang

In Chenjia Hang, Twenty-eighth Tu, in this county, at the home of villager Dai Mao Gou, at about 8 p.m. on the third of this month, someone claimed to be carrying out important business on the orders of the district head, tricked them into opening the gate, and four people entered. Each wore a military cap, uniform, and carried a flashlight and pistol. Zhang Mingshan, who was among those who came, was familiar with the victim and claimed to be there on orders to investigate their trafficking of soil and morphine. The four people searched separately and stole seventeen pieces of cloth, five silver dollars, one paper dollar, and clothing, etc., before leaving. On the fifth, the victim encountered Zhang Mingshan on the road and immediately handed him over to the Sixth Sub-station, asking for him to be dealt with according to the law. He was sent to the general bureau today. According to Dai Mao Gou's confession, he witnessed Zhang Mingshan committing the robbery, but Zhang Mingshan said that he farmed more land than Dai Mao Gou, so how could he commit a robbery? Their confessions differed, so they will be sent to the court for interrogation.

Travelers Commit Double Suicide by Poisoning in Suzhou's First Inn

Yesterday (7th) at 10 a.m., in room 32 of the First Inn outside Lümen, a traveler using the alias Wang Ru Yuan and a female guest Chen Si Bao (real name Gu Si Bao) both committed suicide by poisoning. After the tea attendant discovered this, he reported it to the police, and they were sent to Suyong Hospital for treatment. After Dr. Gu Suyong performed surgery, they are now out of danger, and their lives can be saved. The reporter visited at 12 o'clock, and their minds were clear. According to them, Wang Ru Yuan is his alias, and his real name is Zhang Rui Xian, 27 years old, a local, living at No. 9, Yinfeng Bridge Lane, Shengjia Dai. At the age of seventeen, he became an apprentice at Duanmu Xiang Store, Lianxi Fang in the city. At the age of twenty-two, he was laid off. Through a friend's introduction, he entered the Boxi Hospital in Tianci Zhuang, working as a registrar. He resigned this year in July due to a marriage incident. He met her (Gu Si Bao) in February of this year. They decided to marry each other through friendship. Because her parents did not agree, they could not fulfill their wishes, so they agreed to escape to Wuxi together on July 27 and live together. The eighty yuan they brought out has all been used up. On the fourth, they returned to Suzhou and went to Gu Si Bao's house, but were rejected again. Because of economic pressure and a lack of freedom, they sought death by poisoning. She (Gu Si Bao) is 22 years old, living at No. 12, Zhangjia Lane, Yanzhi Bridge. She has parents and siblings at home. She usually worked at the Zhenfeng Cloth Factory on Shiquan Street. Because they were in love, but not free, they committed suicide together. Now they deeply regret their mistake, etc.

Autopsy Conducted Yesterday in Wuxi's Female Maid Suicide Case

After Zhou Yufen, a female maid at the home of Dr. Zhu Daji, a surgeon in Yangting, was fired by Zhu, she committed suicide by poisoning at No. 43, Park Hotel, and died. The mother of the deceased, Zhou Qu, begged Zhu's family for money to buy a coffin, but was beaten by Zhu's wife and falsely accused of colluding with the tea attendant Tan Genfa to extort money. She was handed over to the local branch for questioning. The prosecutor Lian opened a court to interrogate her. Zhou Qu requested in court that justice be done for her daughter. As a result of the legal autopsy, the court ordered Zhu Daji to be released on bail. Zhou Qu, Zhou He Bao, Zhou Yu Ying, Zhou Xu, Tan Genfa, and others were all ordered to return home. Yesterday (7th) at 10 a.m., the prosecutor Lian, leading the coroner Liu and two bailiffs, took a streetcar to the hostel guild hall. He ordered the undertaker to carry Yufen's body out of the morgue. The coroner Liu performed a legal autopsy. The autopsy revealed that Yufen's entire body was red and swollen, and her fingers and gums were cyanotic. There were several rat bites on her left ear and left fingers. There were several needle marks on both arms from doctors. There were no other abnormalities. It was determined that she had died by poisoning while alive. After the autopsy, he ordered the family of the deceased to prepare a coffin for burial. During the autopsy, Zhou Qu cried bitterly and fainted. Her daughter, Yu Ying, tried her best to wake her up, and the scene was very tragic. It was also heard that the reason for Zhou Yufen's suicide was not due to being fired by Zhu's family. Therefore, the inside story of this case is quite complicated.

Opposing Increased Cotton Yarn Tax, Petitioning in Beijing

The national yarn mill industry has once again dispatched representatives to Beijing to petition against the increase in the unified cotton yarn tax. Shanghai has already designated Guo Shun, Nie Lusheng, Liu Jingji, and Zhang Zemin as representatives, who went to Beijing the night before last. It is learned that the yarn mill industry in this town has also designated Rong Desheng and Xue Mingjian as representatives, who took a train to Beijing at 6:30 a.m. yesterday to join the representatives from Shanghai and petition the Executive Yuan. Peng Xuepei received them on behalf of the Executive Yuan and said that the matter has now been referred to the Ministry of Finance for review and should be decided after the Ministry of Finance has reviewed it. He promised to forward the opinions of the representatives to the President. The representatives were satisfied and left. At noon, they went to the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Finance to petition.

Robbery and Assault Occurs in Changzhou, Near the Outer City

At the home of Gu Genlin in Longku Village, near the outer city of Wuyi First District, at about 1 a.m. on the 5th, more than ten bandits suddenly came, carrying flashlights and sharp weapons. They passed through the wooden planks from the west and smashed through the back door to enter the house. First, they went to Genlin's bedroom, tied Genlin up, and burned his head with fire, forcing him to reveal where he had hidden his money. Then, they rummaged through the boxes and cabinets, stealing more than 300 silver dollars and more than 30 pieces of clothing. After about an hour, they escaped with the stolen goods. On the 6th, the village chief of the village, Wan Jianming, reported the incident to the First District Office, which reported it to the county government for investigation.

Robbery of Coal Shop in Zhoujing, Changshu

Zhoujing Town, Second District, in this county, is located along the Xuliujing River Estuary and is a large market. The market was originally very lively, but due to the drought this year, the market is sluggish. At about 12 p.m. the night before last, more than ten bandits suddenly came to the home of Ma Sanbao, who runs a coal shop on the east side of the town, and robbed the house. Ma's wife did not have time to escape and was immediately kidnapped by the bandits and escaped towards Hupukou. Afterwards, a special force was sent to report to the Meicun Public Security Branch Bureau to pursue them, but the bandits had already gone far away.

Ten pirate ships with more than two hundred pirates in the Qintuan sea area of Lüsi were defeated by the Thirteenth Water Police Team stationed in Tong Province. On the 6th, they fled to Beikan. The Nantong District Security Command immediately dispatched coastal police teams to block and attack them. All coastal areas are under temporary martial law to prevent the bandits from fleeing.

Sentencing Completed in Lujiadong Case

Chen Hai, an apprentice at the Chen Zhusan shoe workshop on Tiexing Road outside the west gate of Tongcheng, sneaked into a nearby farmer's house at night to steal reed straw and was killed in the field. The Public Security Bureau investigated and arrested the murderer and handed him over to the court. On the 6th, the criminal court completed the trial and sentencing. Zhang Libin was sentenced to five years of imprisonment for killing out of righteous indignation on the spot. Song Shou, Song Yao, Chen Hui, and Gu Niang were sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for killing out of righteous indignation on the spot.

The river bordering Jingjiang has been dredged, disputes have arose one after another. Guo Dechao, the director of the Juyi branch office, has ulterior motives. He first moved the lime piles without authorization and encroached on the border. Our branch office reported this to the county government, and the county heads of the two counties, along with Sun Yunxia, a member of the Department of Civil Affairs, went to re-hammer the stakes, and the storm subsided. Director Guo's plan did not succeed, and he later forcibly destroyed the only bridge connecting the two counties, the West Plank Bridge. This bridge had been decided by the two counties to be destroyed and rebuilt after the river dredging was completed. Now Guo has forcibly destroyed it in violation of the order, which has caused another storm, and all river dredging has been stopped. Our county head Li has telegraphed the special commissioner's office to send an engineer to supervise the work as soon as possible to avoid disputes from arising from time to time.

In Langshi Town, Nanxin Di, Fourth District of Huaiyin, a farmer surnamed Li had an argument with Wang Yinhuai, the village head, on the 3rd. The Central Government's Finances Can Safely Pass the End of the Year

News from Banking Circles in This City

According to news from banking circles in this city from the Central News Agency, since Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi took office, he has worked diligently on increasing revenue and reducing expenditure. The income and expenditure can now be balanced. However, it is inevitable that there will be some difficulties at the end of each year. But for this year, there is no problem with the central government's finances. The Ministry of Finance has sold the stamp tax to the China Construction Bank Corporation at a 93% discount, obtaining a total of 30 million yuan. This amount is more than enough to safely pass the end of this year. Furthermore, since the Ministry of Finance increased the silver export tax and equalization tax, silver exports have virtually ceased. As for tax evasion and smuggling, the Ministry of Finance has joined forces with military and police agencies to strictly prevent it. Therefore, the money market has gradually eased. Yesterday, the interbank lending rate was 23%.

Fenghua Fellow Villagers Association Cables Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Yesterday

Requesting Disaster Relief for Zhejiang

This year, the drought in Zhejiang has affected 47 counties, with nearly 2.5 million victims. The old, weak, women, and children are suffering from hunger and cold, and are wandering everywhere. The situation is too terrible to bear. Currently, as it is the dead of winter, the situation is becoming more serious. Citizens from all counties in Zhejiang have telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, pleading for the relief of their hometowns and disaster victims, and requesting the Zhejiang Provincial Government to release the one million relief funds allocated from provincial bonds as soon as possible to benefit the disaster victims. Yesterday, Mr. Wu Zhihao of the Fenghua Fellow Villagers Association also telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting the simultaneous organization of emergency relief and work relief. The original telegram is recorded below: "Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, Sir: The drought in Zhejiang this year is extremely severe. According to investigation reports, 47 counties are disaster areas with over 2.5 million disaster victims who cannot survive without relief. The majority are old, weak, women, and children, suffering from hunger and cold, wandering everywhere. Grass roots and tree bark have been exhausted, and people are starving to death and committing suicide in increasing numbers. The current situation in the disaster area is too terrible to bear. They are crying for food and urgently hoping for relief. Collecting relief funds is a drop in the bucket. The counties are sending urgent requests, and the relief personnel have no rice to cook. The Zhejiang Relief Conference has decided to allocate one million from the Zhejiang Provincial Bonds to provide emergency relief first, saving the disaster victims who are old, weak, women, and children from dying by sunset, and then organize work relief, enabling the strong to replace relief with labor and build a foundation for fundamental disaster relief. You, sir, care about your hometown and have compassion for the disaster victims. Please immediately telegraph the Zhejiang Provincial Government to organize emergency relief and work relief simultaneously. The disaster victims in Zhejiang will be fortunate to have a day of revival. All of this will be your everlasting merit. We earnestly hope for your telegram as much as a severe drought hopes for clouds. On behalf of the disaster victims, we respectfully offer incense and pray. We eagerly await your instructions." Wu Zhihao of the Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association of Fenghua bows.

The details of the day are translated and recorded below:

Attendees: The attendees that day were mostly celebrities in Shanghai, including Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, former Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, Zhang Gongquan, Du Yuesheng, Li Ming, Lin Kanghou, Song Ziliang, etc.

Wang and Wu Deliver Speeches: After the meeting began, Wang Zhengting first delivered an introductory speech, stating briefly that the relationship between China and Britain is extremely close. Although Britain is far from the East, it has many colonies in the Pacific, so the relationship is quite deep. This time, Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen has done an excellent job in allocating the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity funds, so that China can receive practical assistance in various fields such as shipping, education, and railways. This belief is that both China and Britain will obtain closer friendship under Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen's efforts. The British Ambassador has recently inspected various parts of China and has a thorough understanding of the construction efforts in various parts of China. As for the construction work in Shanghai, it is only a small part of the whole country. In the future, the Chinese government is striving to actively develop the national construction undertaking.

Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen's Speech: I have been in China for a short time and have not seen much. I have not been able to gain a deep understanding of the situation in China. What I can say today is only what I know from my personal experience and offer it as a contribution. When I first arrived in China, the situation in the Far East had become stable. I firmly believe that it will become more and more peaceful in the future. China's foreign diplomacy has not reached a serious stage this year. China internally is now relatively peaceful. During this peaceful period, the Chinese government can fully focus on domestic enrichment and construction. However, to achieve China's strength, it must make long-term efforts. What China should pay special attention to during this period is how to seek mutual cooperation with the international community. No country can achieve prosperity by breaking away from international relations. As for China internally, there is even more need for cooperation with the international community, because China cannot develop externally without first uniting internally. This point is not based on the concept of the state. This cooperation requires every member to contribute their personal strength to the country in order to achieve the health of the entire country. China's only cure is not to copy foreigners blindly. It should use its inherent spirit to extract the strengths of foreigners to make up for its own shortcomings. This is the significance of China's need to cooperate with the international community. I believe that any country will be happy to accept this. The current global recession is coming to an end. Although the British domestic economy has stabilized through the efforts of the British people, the future development of Britain cannot be achieved by Britain alone. It also needs the cooperation of other countries in order to achieve the goal of coexistence and co-prosperity.

Chairman Xu Shiying reported on telegrams from various places requesting relief and the quantity of donations and relief supplies received, records from the previous meeting, and the situation of contacting relief affairs in Beijing. Then, the two groups in charge of design and investigation reported on the review and statistics situation.

The resolution of various cases was immediately followed by a discussion, including: (1) The principle of relief methods was discussed and approved. (2) The current weather is getting colder. How should the cotton clothes received by the Society be distributed and released? It was decided that the distribution would be made after the investigation director's investigation report. (3) Fujian Province has also suffered from drought this year. Li Wanzhong, the magistrate of Putian County and chairman of the Charity Relief Association, has sent a letter requesting relief. Should it be added? It was resolved to be added. (4) Mr. Zhang Yongni sent a letter stating that Qingjiang Congee Factory is doing a conscientious job. This year, due to the drought, there are many people who need food, and the price of rice is expensive. It is very difficult. Please allocate a sum of 1,000 or 2,000 yuan from the aviation funds to provide relief. It was resolved to allocate 1,000 yuan. Temporary proposals were then discussed, including: (1) Detailed investigation and distribution rules. It was decided that the investigation and distribution group would draft them. (2) Recognition of the design group's resolution. (A) Forward a letter to the Banking Association, urging all money shops to organize relief and loan departments in the disaster area. (B) First send a letter to the Exchange to inquire about the number of disaster relief bonds issued. If there are any that have not been issued, please ask the central government to issue public bonds and change them to 100 million yuan. The public bond fund is guaranteed by customs surcharges. The public bonds are to be kept and managed by the Relief Committee.

The relief method was passed yesterday. The original text of the investigation and emergency relief methods is as follows: (1) The standard for relief distribution is that the disaster-stricken area is 60% or more of the total. The standard is to be investigated by the Investigation Director of the Society in conjunction with the provincial governments and provincial relief committees, submitted to the Society for approval. The standard for beneficiaries is extreme poverty, being 50 years or older, 15 years or younger, or having disabilities and other conditions that make it impossible to survive without relief. (2) The Society will conduct the investigation and distribution directly. (3) The principle of relief distribution is food distribution, with each person receiving approximately 2 yuan of relief grain. If there is a need to increase or decrease the amount, the Investigation Director may make temporary adjustments and report to the Society. (4) Each province will have an Investigation Director, named Shanghai Fundraising Society for Drought Relief in Various Provinces, Investigation Director of a certain province (city). Under the Director, staff may be employed. Each county that should receive relief may have a county Investigation Director and staff. (5) Relief distribution will use the Society's relief tickets, stamped with the joint distribution mark of the Central Disaster Area Multi-Term Emergency Relief Committee. The person who distributes the relief supplies or relief funds by the Society shall use this relief ticket. (6) The Society shall send personnel to distribute relief and report to the central government to send personnel for supervision. (7) The relief procedures shall be the responsibility of the Investigation Director of the Society for investigation and ticket distribution. All relief supplies and relief funds shall be publicly distributed by the local government relief associations with the relief ticket, and the relief ticket shall be collected. The local government relief branches shall issue a certificate of proof and hand it over to the Investigation Director of the Society for transfer to the Society, which shall hand it over to the accountant for review. After the review, it shall be submitted to the central government and the Relief Committee of the National Government for record. (8) All internal expenses of the Society shall be raised separately and shall not use relief funds. As for the relief distribution expenses of each province (city), the expenses shall be cut from the relief funds according to the official and charity relief precedents. The proportion shall be specified in the detailed investigation and distribution rules. (9) After the Investigation Director of each province (city) receives the relief funds and supplies, he/she shall store them in the bank designated by the provincial government and provincial relief association when arriving at each province (city) and wait for distribution. The relief supplies shall be stored in a designated public storage area. (10) The Investigation Director of each province (city) shall, upon arrival at the location, formulate a concrete plan for relief distribution in the province (city) and the actual situation of the current relief work in conjunction with the provincial government and provincial relief association and submit it to the Society for verification, and report the daily work to the Society on a weekly basis. (11) Detailed investigation and distribution rules shall be formulated separately.

Statement of Opinions: Xu Shiying, the vice president of the Society, submitted a written opinion to the Central Winter Emergency Relief Association on the winter emergency relief measures for the disaster area. Now, the central relief funds decided by the Ba Feng Conference shall be requested for approval by the Society. The original statement is as follows: (1) Relief standards. (A) Standards for relief areas. (1) If the number of disaster-stricken counties in a province accounts for more than 50% of the total number, or the disaster-stricken fields in a city account for more than 50% of the total area of the city's fields, the central government shall directly organize emergency relief. (2) In the provinces directly administered by the central government for relief, relief shall only be provided if the disaster-stricken fields in a county account for more than 70% of the total area of the county's fields. (3) If the number of disaster-stricken counties does not meet the standards for direct relief by the central government, the central government shall provide appropriate subsidies, and the relief funds shall be handed over to the provincial government, provincial party headquarters, and provincial relief committee for joint responsibility. A special report shall be submitted, but the disaster-stricken counties and population, as well as the investigation and distribution methods, shall comply with the standards for direct relief by the central government. (B) Standards for relief population. (2) The extremely poor people, aged 55 or older, 12 or younger, or those who lack self-help ability due to fatigue, disability, or other circumstances, shall be given emergency relief on a per capita basis. (3) Investigation and distribution methods. (A) The county government, county party headquarters, and county relief branch shall conduct a preliminary investigation and compile a roster of disaster victims. (B) The investigation director and deputy director shall send personnel to conduct a joint review with the county government, county party headquarters, county relief branch, and local public groups to issue relief tickets. (C) The investigation director and deputy director shall send personnel to conduct a joint review with the county government, county party headquarters, county relief branch, and representatives of local public groups to exchange relief goods or relief funds according to the relief tickets (soup kitchens may be set up if necessary). (D) The county relief offices shall be responsible for compiling and sending the disaster relief rosters and documents, and the association shall collect and submit them to the central government for verification. (E) After the relief work is completed, the central government shall select commissioners to go to the relief areas to conduct spot checks on the ground in order to ensure that the benefits reach the people. (F) The provincial investigation director shall be selected and appointed by the central government, and the deputy director shall be appointed by the provincial government. (G) The emergency relief mentioned above shall be based on the distribution of relief grain, but in areas with inconvenient transportation and difficult transportation, relief funds may be distributed appropriately.

National Economic Commission Repairs Ningxia Water Conservancy

Appropriates 200,000 Yuan to Dredge the Yunting Canal

Irrigates 600,000 Mu of Land, Can Establish Another County

According to the National News Agency in Shanghai, the National Economic Commission is repairing Ningxia water conservancy. The 15th Route Army soldiers are dredging the Yunting Canal. According to a report from the technical personnel stationed in Ningxia by the Water Conservancy Department of the Commission, the 15th Route Army soldiers are excavating the Yunting Canal. The canal mouth to Wangzhuang is divided into seven sections. The first and second sections each have 1,500 soldiers, the third and fourth sections each have 1,600 soldiers, the fifth section has 1,500 soldiers, the sixth section has 1,800 soldiers, and the seventh section has 2,200 soldiers, totaling 11,700 soldiers. They started working along the line from the 1st of this month, starting work at 7:00 AM every day, having lunch at 12:00 noon, and stopping work for dinner at 5:00 PM. When there is moonlight, they work at night for two or three hours. The regimental commanders personally supervise them. All officers and soldiers are able to work bravely and without slackening. Therefore, they have completed the work in a short period of time. The first section was completed on the 28th of this month, the second section was completed on the 21st, the third, fourth, fifth, and sixth sections were completed on the 18th, and the seventh section was completed on the 20th. All construction plans are formulated by the Construction Department in accordance with the rules of the National Economic Commission, and personnel are sent to each section to be responsible for guidance. As for the section from Wangzhuang to the end of the canal, the work must be continued next spring because the weather is too cold now. The canal's expenses, excluding the soldiers, are only 200,000 yuan allocated by the National Economic Commission. After the canal is completed, it can irrigate approximately 600,000 mu of land and can establish another county.

Yesterday Morning, the Beifu Collided with the Hua'an in the Huangpu River

Hua'an Enters Factory for Repairs

This Matter Has Already Concluded

The Northern Shipping Company's Beifu, originating from North China, arrived in Shanghai and docked at the Datong Wharf in the southern section of the Huangpu River to unload cargo. Yesterday morning at around 10:00 AM, the cargo having been cleared, it needed to head to the Zhoujiadu Wharf in Pudong to load cargo. It immediately departed from Datong Wharf and began to turn its hull. Unexpectedly, an unfortunate incident occurred.

To Avoid a Ferry, the Captain of the Beifu Was a White Russian Named Guxin Cuofu. As the ship turned, he noticed a ferry coming from Gaochang Temple to Zhoujiadu, fully loaded with seventy or eighty passengers, approaching the Beifu's side. By this time, the Beifu had already moved away from the wharf and was turning. In the center of the Huangpu River was the Navy's transport ship, the Hua'an. If the Beifu avoided the Hua'an, it would inevitably sink the ferry, and all the passengers would drown. Considering the lesser of two evils, the captain had no choice but to yield to the ferry and collide with the Hua'an transport ship to avoid a major tragedy.

The Hua'an Was Hit. The Beifu crashed violently into the Hua'an's port-side iron plating. The iron plates of the Hua'an transport ship were damaged, a portion dented inward, and a portion broken by the Beifu. The damage was at the waterline, so river water immediately entered the ship. Fortunately, the breach was not large, so it was possible to devise a way to plug the gap and repair it.

Three-Party Joint Inspection. After the incident, the Beifu argued that to preserve the lives of the ferry's passengers, it had to yield, resulting in the collision with the Hua'an. However, the Hua'an was anchored in the river, so the responsibility for the accident rested with the Beifu, which was not in question. As for the damage, after the captain of the Beifu reported to the company, the company, together with the Navy authorities, requested a fair-minded person yesterday to conduct an inspection of the damage to the Hua'an transport ship. The Navy immediately sent the Hua'an to the factory for repairs. The responsible party will pay all repair costs. This matter has already been concluded. The Beifu did not suffer any damage and departed for the Laoyao area of Haizhou yesterday.

Longshan Shipowner Telegraphs That Japanese Navy Has Understood

Still Going to Saigon to Load Rice

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Longshan, belonging to the Sanbei Shipping Company, was en route to Saigon to load foreign rice ordered by Chinese merchants when it was struck by a hurricane off Keelung, northern Taiwan, a few days ago. It sent a telegram requesting assistance. After escaping from the hurricane, the shipowner, Leisibei, discovered that seawater had entered the hold, and he anchored there to pump out the water. However, as the location was a Japanese naval port, the stationed Japanese warship summoned the shipowner for questioning. The ship telegraphed Shanghai to report. After the general manager of Sanbei Company, Yu Qiaqing, sent a telegram, he received a telegram from the Longshan shipowner yesterday morning, informing him that they had obtained the understanding of the Japanese warship and would proceed to Saigon to load foreign rice as planned. The water in the ship has been pumped out. After inspection, although it was hit by a hurricane, it fortunately suffered no damage.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Submits to the Municipal Government for Amendment of the Regulations Restricting Brokerage

Various Industries Jointly State Their Difficulties

Please Promulgate the Compromise Solution Immediately

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce submitted to the Municipal Government yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of submitting a request, on the 6th of this month, we received a joint letter from the following trade associations: Fruit and Produce Industry, Seafood and Sundries Industry, Bean and Rice Industry, Coarse Grain and Oilcake Industry, Medicinal Materials Industry, Fresh Pork Industry, Liang Shaojiu Industry, Timber Industry, Charcoal Industry, Green Bamboo Shoots Industry, Salted Fish Industry, Chicken and Duck Industry, Miscellaneous Firewood Industry, Produce Industry, Southern Goods Industry, Cured Meat Industry, Fresh Fish Industry, Northern Goods Industry, etc., stating that since the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau announced the Brokerage Business Regulations on August 30th of this year, all those engaged in brokerage business have been alarmed and distraught. The affiliated associations have repeatedly requested the Chamber to present the case based on reason, industry customs, and the Social Bureau's approval, and to postpone the implementation of the new regulations to ensure that commercial practices and legal principles are considered. The Chamber dispatched Standing Committee Member Jin Runxiang and Committee Member Ma Shaoquan, together with representatives from various industries, including Gu Xinyi, Cai Runshan, Xin Wenyao, Ni Baizhai, Rao Hanzhang, and others, to petition the Municipal Government. Secretary-General Yu personally instructed them to draft a memorandum outlining the difficulties of each industry and submit it to the Government for review and a proper solution to alleviate the merchants' plight. The affiliated associations have separately drafted memorandums and requested the Chamber to forward them to the Municipal Government for review and decision. Nearly a month has passed, and no response has been received from the Municipal Government, leaving the brokers in a state of confusion and uncertainty. It is noted that the business regulations announced by the Finance Bureau this time have changed the usual practice and are based on the seven-point plan for reorganizing brokerage taxes decided by the National Financial Conference issued by the Ministry of Finance. However, Item 3 of the reorganization plan, which restricts brokerage commissions, states that brokerage commissions vary greatly from province to province, ranging from 1% to 5%. Given the current difficulties of agriculture and commerce and the decline in commodity prices, it seems appropriate to impose restrictions, proposing to set a limit of 3%, to be determined by each province and city based on the local trading conditions. The reason for the restriction is nothing more than the inconsistency of the rates charged in various provinces and cities, coupled with the difficulties of agriculture and commerce and the decline in commodity prices. However, the commissions charged by brokers are mostly based on the amount of the transaction. As commodity prices fall, the amount of the transaction also falls, and the commissions charged by brokers also decrease accordingly. It is clear that the difficulties of agriculture and commerce are affected by the decline in commodity prices, not by the amount of the commissions. If the commissions charged by brokers vary greatly from province to province and should be restricted to achieve uniformity, then the trading conditions in each province and city are different, and the rights and obligations of the parties involved in the transactions are also different. The amount of commissions set by each industry is based on the mutual rights and obligations of the parties involved and has been agreed upon by all parties concerned for a long time. Moreover, the economic life of urban areas cannot be compared with the economic life of rural areas. Since the economic conditions of each province and city vary, and the brokerage commissions on which brokers depend for their livelihood are mostly 10% in Shanghai, imposing a uniform restriction would be like cutting off the feet to fit the shoes, putting the brokers in Shanghai to death. However, the last paragraph of the annotation to Item 3, which states that 'commodity prices are falling and restrictions should be imposed, proposing to set a limit of 3%, to be determined by each province and city based on the local trading conditions,' implies that the right to impose restrictions is flexible and can be adjusted freely by each province and city. The Finance Bureau should follow the industry regulations approved by the Social Bureau and separately stipulate the commissions to maintain the industry's inherent customs and secure livelihoods. As for Item 4, the brokerage business tax should be based on the amount of the transaction or the amount of the commission (omitted). If it is collected based on the amount of the transaction, the tax rate should not exceed 3%. If it is based on the amount of the commission, the tax rate should not exceed 20%. In the future, if brokerage businesses are taxed at a rate of 3% based on the amount of the transaction, and brokers comply with Item 3 of the regulations and charge brokerage commissions that are equivalent to the amount of the tax, then the establishment of brokerage businesses would seem to be a tax collection agency, and the brokers themselves would have no means of support. Such a high tax rate and such a restriction on brokerage commissions would surely cause the conference participants to cry out on behalf of the brokers if they carefully reviewed the matter. If it is thought that brokers must be subject to a very heavy business tax, then it would also violate the highest tax rate of the business tax law. However, the Shanghai brokerage business regulations stipulate that the minimum fixed tax cannot be based on the amount of the transaction. Whether or not this fixed rate will be changed in Shanghai should be clearly indicated by the Finance Bureau to reassure the merchants. The affiliated associations have previously stated some of the above points, but there are still some unexpressed concerns. We respectfully submit this joint petition again and request the Chamber to promptly forward it to the Municipal Government to adopt the difficulties raised in the memorandums of the various industries and to quickly issue an improved solution to alleviate the merchants' plight. The Chamber has repeatedly forwarded to your Government the various statements and memorandums submitted by the industries, requesting a compromise solution. Regarding Item 3 of the National Financial Conference's plan for reorganizing brokerage taxes, which states that 'brokerage commissions vary greatly from province to province, ranging from 1% to 5%,' the situation in Shanghai is significantly higher than the so-called 5%. This has been repeatedly stated and need not be repeated. Shanghai is the largest commercial center in the country, and the original plan is so divorced from reality. It is clear that the plan was not based on an actual investigation before the discussion, and it is inappropriate to use it as a standard for restriction. First, the business relationship between merchants is purely a mutual contract between merchants. If it does not harm public order, the state should not interfere excessively. The National Financial Conference's restriction on brokerage commissions is based on the pretext of falling commodity prices. This argument is inappropriate, as detailed in the Chamber's rebuttal. If, as it is said, brokerage commissions are a certain percentage of the price of the goods, then if commodity prices fall, the fixed percentage of the brokerage commission will inevitably fall accordingly. The fall in commodity prices is the cause, and the fall in brokerage commissions is the effect. The state has not restricted commodity prices, which are following the natural trend, but has restricted brokerage commissions alone, which is inappropriate. Moreover, because brokerage commissions are falling due to the fall in commodity prices, merchants are already suffering losses implicitly. If a fixed percentage that does not correspond to the facts is now imposed, wouldn't they be suffering a double loss? Second, based on the above supplementary reasons, we respectfully submit this document again to your Government for review and approval, and we ask that the compromise solution be approved and announced immediately for the convenience of the public."

Coin Exhibition Opens Today

Displaying More Than 2,700 Kinds of Coins

Exhibition at the New World Hotel for Two Days

Financial figures Wang Shouqian and Ping Yulin, in view of the fact that China has had silver coins for more than 3,000 years, and there are many types of coins in various dynasties, in order to enable the Chinese people to understand the coinage system of various dynasties, have specially decided to publicly exhibit the precious coins purchased and stored with private funds from today to the 9th at Room 324, 3rd Floor, New World Hotel, Nanjing Road, and named it the Rare Chinese Gold, Silver, and Copper Coin Exhibition. According to Mr. Ping Yulin of the Industrial Society, the motive for launching this exhibition is that museums in various countries around the world have coin displays, and many have also collected Chinese coins, spending tens of millions of dollars to enable the public to understand the coinage systems of various countries. However, China has been lacking in this regard for thousands of years, which is regrettable. This time, colleagues have launched an exhibition to display a total of more than 2,700 kinds of coins, all of which are Chinese coins from various dynasties and are rare in society. However, due to the limited capabilities of colleagues, they cannot go to various provinces and cities to hold public exhibitions. They hope that the central authorities will pay close attention to coin displays.

Enthusiastic Reservations for "Scenic Southeast"

The book "Scenic Southeast" was compiled for the Southeast Five Provinces Tour. At the beginning of the compilation, the Zhejiang Construction Department invited famous domestic artists to tour a week according to the planned route, and then wrote it into text and attached it with pictures. It took half a year and cost a lot of money. The materials in the book are centered on Zhejiang Province, slightly extending to the provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Fujian, and Jiangxi bordering Zhejiang. The scenery of Zhejiang Province, such as the peaks of Yandang, the waterfalls of Tiantai, the ancient trees of Tianmu, and the majestic pass of Xianxia, as well as the cliffs of Xuedou Fangyan and the caves of Beishan Shimen, is relatively complete. The entire book is exquisitely printed on copperplate paper, measuring 10.5 inches wide and 14 inches high, and bound into a large volume. With this book, the scenic spots of Southeast China can be seen at a glance. The book is scheduled to be published on January 1, 1935, and reservations have now begun. The price of the book is eight yuan, but reservations only cost four yuan. Cause of the Shanghai-Taicang Staff's Work Slowdown

The Reason Is the Retention of Free Travel Passes

The Public Security Bureau Illegally Arrested a Ticket Inspector

Yesterday (Thursday) at 12:00 noon, when the Shanghai-Taicang long-distance bus company's fourth bus from Shanghai to Jiading passed through the Dachang station, an inspector in plain clothes boarded the bus and arrived at Liuhang, and carried out an inspection at Liuhang station. At that time, all the passengers on the bus questioned the inspector's right to carry out an inspection in plain clothes and without a badge. Later, the inspector claimed to be a member of the Opium Prohibition Committee and detained one male and one female passenger, taking them to the Liuhang Public Security Substation. They were released immediately after it was found that there were no prohibited items. After arriving at Liuhang, the inspector returned to Baoshan by bus. Station staff Xu Zixiang boarded the bus to check tickets. The inspector presented a free travel pass for the Dachang Public Security Bureau issued by the Shanghai-Taicang Company, but station staff Xu Zixiang, because he was in plain clothes and had no badge, believed that it did not comply with the company's regulations and retained the pass. He then asked the company for instructions. Unexpectedly, the inspector also reported to Zhou Jintang, the director of the Dachang Public Security Bureau, by telephone, and sent five armed police officers, carrying ropes, to rush to Liuhang station, bind Xu, and take him back to Dachang, and then transfer him to Baoshan. It is now known that the company believes that the free travel pass is to provide preferential treatment to maintain local security and charitable and cultural organizations and cannot be considered a due right. When using it, they should abide by the company's regulations. Since the inspector did not use it in accordance with the regulations, he illegally bound the station staff as if arresting bandits. Therefore, the company's staff became dissatisfied and triggered a strike. Yesterday, some of the staff on the Songhu Line declared a work slowdown, believing that unless the perpetrator is punished, it would not be enough to warn others. However, according to news from the Baoshan County Government, Xu Zixiang has been released and ordered to investigate and deal with the matter according to law.

Port Authority Dredges New Waterway of Huangpu River

Located near Gaoqiao and Zhanghuabang

Dredged to a width of 300 feet and a length of over 5,000 feet

Two marker ships set up starting yesterday

The Jianghai Customs Port Authority, starting from the 1st of this month, is re-dredging the new waterway area of the Huangpu River to a width of 300 English feet to facilitate the passage of incoming and outgoing ships. Starting today, two marker ships will be set up there to indicate the depth scale on the Puxi side during low tide. Our Datong News Agency reporter has explored and recorded the details below:

Evolution of the New Waterway: A Datong News Agency reporter inquired with the Customs yesterday morning and learned that this new waterway area is opposite Gaoqiao Sand, near Zhanghuabang. This water area was only newly opened more than ten years ago. Previously, the water flow of the Huangpu River was still on the east side of the new waterway. Later, after the Port Authority's measurements, it was recognized that the old waterway was hindering navigation and water conservancy, so the Dredging Bureau dredged it over a long period. However, now that the number of incoming and outgoing ships is increasing daily, the Port Authority believes it is necessary to continue to widen the new waterway of the Huangpu River.

It was found that Detaille is supervising the dredging to a width of 300 feet and a length of approximately 5,600 feet. The Hailong No. 2 dredger of the Dredging Bureau has started dredging work since the 1st of this month. In recent days, the Chief Engineer of the Dredging Bureau, together with the surveying and dredging personnel, has been supervising the work. The Hailong No. 2 dredger is still new and has a dredging capacity of about 500 to 600 tons per hour. However, when working, due to the need to avoid passing ships, the dredging time is inevitably affected to a considerable extent. Therefore, it is currently impossible to estimate how long it will take to complete the project.

Attention of Ships: During the dredging period, ships passing through this area must slowly sail closer to the Puxi side. If they approach the dredger, they must sound a long signal so that the dredger has sufficient time to loosen its side anchor cables to avoid accidents. As for the relevant signals, all customs' usual berthing signals and lights shall be followed.

Setting up New Markers: The Port Authority Director, Valienne, has issued another notice for setting up marker ships in the area, which roughly states: "Regarding the periodic implementation of dredging the new waterway of the Huangpu River, to designate the boundaries of the navigable waterway starting tomorrow, two marker ships will be set up there starting December 7th of this year. These ships are used to indicate the 18-foot isobath of the Huangpu River on the Puxi side during low tide. One will be berthed downstream of the dredger, approximately 1,500 feet from the ship, and the other will be berthed upstream of the dredger, also 1,500 feet from the ship. Each marker will have the Shanghai Dredging Bureau flag on top of the mast during the day, and two white lights, spaced approximately six feet apart, at night. These lights will be visible at least one mile within the surrounding horizon in clear weather," etc.

Rent Reduction Committee Resolves Yesterday to Send Representatives

To Petition the Fifth Plenary Session

The Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee held its 32nd executive, design, law, and joint meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. Over 20 people attended, including Qiu Liangyu, Qiu Jialiang, Wang Jingdong, Zhou Fuzhang, Zhang Xianfang, Li Ruzhang, Ren Nongxuan, Zhang Yichen, Liu Zhongying, Hu Fengxiang, etc. Zhang Yichen was elected as the chairman and Liang Gengshun as the recorder. After the report, the following cases were discussed: (1) The case of realizing rent reduction to save merchants in distress was resolved: (A) Wang Jingdong and Hu Fengxiang were elected as petition representatives to go to Beijing immediately; (B) A petition will be submitted to the Fifth Plenary Session. (2) The case of the rent for Lao Qichang's Henglong Bingdian was resolved to be handed over to the investigation section for investigation. (3) Wang Xingyi's suggestion to invite comedic masters Liu Chunshan and others to broadcast propaganda for rent reduction was resolved to be notified for publicity separately. (4) The case of how to stop the Nanshi Rent Reduction Special Issue from charging fees with the "subsidy fee" designation was resolved to notify all branch offices to stop it uniformly to maintain the credibility of rent reduction. (5) The case of how to accelerate the rent reduction work was resolved to nominate Zhang Xianfang and Liu Zhongying to prepare a plan for discussion at the next joint meeting.
