Spring and Autumn

Little Western Heaven

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Fawning Laughter Meets Lamp Illuminates, Careworn Hungry Gut Drives Painted Wind and Flow

Fortunately, there was a teapot on the table. After pouring it out, the two of them drank it all. Only then did Little Ji come in smiling, carrying many things, and when she put them on the table and looked, there were washbasins, towels, mirrors, soap boxes, snow creams, powder boxes, and rouge creams. He said to Aunt Hu: "You dress her up." After saying that, she ran out and brought in a pot of hot water. She ran out again and brought in a package of clothes. Seeing that Yueying was still sitting upright and proper, she straightened her face and said, "Little girl, why don't you do something? You need to know that running around like this is all for you, and it's not that I'm greedy for any benefits. I want to say something that is not very considerate, if you had a way, would you have made me, a tea room worker, send you these pot pieces that you've already eaten?" Yueying couldn't help but blush when she heard this. Aunt Hu said, "Did you even have to say that? Our young lady has some pride, but because she was too hungry yesterday, and there was really no way, she barely came this morning." Little Ji said, "Here you come again. Since you've come, of course you're hoping that things will be successful. Wash your face, change your clothes, and let people be happy when they see you, wouldn't that be good? If you feel embarrassed with me here, I'll leave. That Master Jia is probably up. Maybe he'll go out in the morning, you better go a little earlier." Saying that, he closed the door for them and left first. Aunt Hu said, "Yueying, there's a mirror here, you can do it yourself." Yueying frowned and said, "If that's the case, wouldn't I become someone who sells flirtations? Auntie, you think, I'm already ashamed to death by showing my face like this, and if I dress up for people to see, where would I put this face of mine?" Aunt Hu said, "Who doesn't say that? But you have to think that if it wasn't for thickening this face today, we wouldn't have these pot pieces to eat. You also have to remember that there are two people at home who must be starving for who knows how long. We're still counting on Little Ji's dollar." (84)

In Memory of Mr. Shi Liangcai

— Wo Fo

Originally, Mr. Shi Liangcai and I had no ties of hometown, kinship, family friendship, scholarly association, or personal friendship. I originally did not need to announce my grief for Mr. Shi, which I kept in my heart, to the world through writing. However, the assassination of Mr. Shi this time has given me such deep feelings. In order to express these feelings, I cannot help but write this article.

Mr. Shi's assassination this time is truly worthy of mourning, and at the same time, it is most worthy of admiration. On the other hand, it makes people feel endless emotion; because Mr. Shi could have avoided being assassinated, Mr. Shi's assassination this time can also be said to be self-inflicted. However, this point is precisely Mr. Shi's extraordinary greatness.

The only principle that Chinese people hold is enjoyment. Therefore, as long as they can escape the environment of struggle and shouting in their lives, they will live in seclusion, enjoying the material pleasures in a leisurely and comfortable manner. No matter how much the country needs them, how much society needs them, or how much public welfare undertakings need them, they are always unwilling to adapt to the needs, to step into the world and shoulder their responsibilities, and to exert their abilities. This principle is certainly advantageous and victorious for them personally, but what kind of obstacles will it bring to the country, society, public welfare undertakings, and other aspects? Now, Mr. Shi is different. Considering his position and wealth, he could have lived comfortably in an ivory tower, enjoying a life of ease. Moreover, Mr. Shi had already made great contributions in the past, so even if he enjoyed himself in the future, he would have lived up to the country, society, and public welfare undertakings. However, Mr. Shi always broke away from individualism and always served the public. Even a wealthy person would not sit under a dangerous wall, but Mr. Shi still tirelessly toiled in the world. Although Mr. Shi's assassination may have been due to his unwillingness to enjoy himself and his dedication to service, Mr. Shi's spirit of preferring service and not fearing assassination is truly admirable.

Finally, I think Mr. Shi's assassination may be because there are too few people like Mr. Shi in this society. Alas!

A Meng and the Green Peony

— Qing Qu

The green peony is a rare flower among chrysanthemums; because this kind of chrysanthemum has very wide petals, a very large flower head, and especially its color, which is a deep green with a touch of deep blue, and the flower pistils are even more green and vibrant, which is its characteristic; like the Caotang in Luxu, the Ancient Flower Tower of the Hu family in Chengxiang, the Salt Warehouse in Nanli, and the Ruizhi Righteous Village outside Ximen, although there are many varieties, none of them are as good as the chrysanthemum in the Municipal Junior Middle School in the North Gate, which once gained a reputation for its campus gardening just because of this pot of green peony!

The school has been growing chrysanthemums for many years, but is the planting and irrigation entrusted to a florist? Not exactly, but it is entrusted to one of the school's janitors, and to achieve this result is really not easy! This janitor is called A Meng by everyone in the school, and the name of Xin A Meng is well known even outside the school; because he is very loyal to his duties and has never made any mistakes that people can criticize, the chrysanthemums he grows are exceptionally beautiful and famous, so everyone attributes the credit to A Meng; some people say, "A Meng" can be called a chrysanthemum slave, because he is already over fifty years old, and all his teeth have fallen out, and the male and female students in the school all call him an old woman. However, A Meng often pursed his lips and said when he heard this: "Old woman, you! Look at the chrysanthemums I grow, aren't they like seventeen or eighteen-year-old young men and modern ladies?"

This time, the green peony, introduced by a certain gentleman, participated in the Qingyang Port Chrysanthemum Exhibition and took the first place. A Meng naturally heard this news and couldn't help but smile happily; alas! Who knew that when this pot of green peony went out, it had a total of thirteen flowers in good order, but when it returned, in the eyes of others, it just looked like a student who had won the final victory in the sports field and returned triumphantly; A Meng planted this pot of green peony with his own hands, and in his heart, it was like his own son. He took a close look at the green peony and couldn't help but sigh and say: "Why are there only twelve flowers now out of thirteen flowers?" He was almost so anxious that tears were about to fall; recently, when someone asked about the green peony, he still grumbled that people really had no public virtue!

Song of the Sweater Dog

— Shan Gong

Seen on North Sichuan Road

Strange things in the world are everywhere, just look at today's sweater dog, how lucky the dog is to wear a sweater, it should know to follow the master's great kindness, a modern Chinese girl, holding a dog walking on the street, she kindly made cold clothes for it in the cold weather, knitting a sweater with delicate hands, an overcoat is ironed and draped over it, tightly tied at the waist with buttons, in the past, I heard that there were monkeys rewarded with purple robes, dogs are also eager to be first, how can they be willing to lag behind, the dog now wears grace and jumps wildly, either first or last, left or right, the owner is also not lonely, walking forward, looking back. Alas, this year the world is in turmoil, poor people are carrying burdens selling their children, their voices are hoarse and exhausted, enduring cold and hunger, but the dog is full of beef and tired of chewing, it is like finding people and dogs posting advertisements, the price of people is not as high as the price of dogs, can a person be inferior to a dog, who can detail the reason for this, love it and want to add it to the knee, and be more adorned with beautiful clothes as a spectacle, dog, dog, unparalleled encounter, praise your master for endless blessings. I heard that the ancients valued universal love, treating people with benevolence and loving creatures, why is it reasonable to despise people and value animals, heaven and earth have no use to lightly sigh, alas! Strange things in the world are everywhere, just look at today's sweater dog.

It has been more than ten days since the day that Premier Shi was killed. God is silent, where can the wise find solace? I am filled with grief and despair.

The Fragrant Shadows of the Imperial Palace

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling, Translated by Qin Shouou

Leaving the second courtyard, we entered the third courtyard. Everyone who went in here was careful to restrain themselves, not daring to make any noise. Because the relics stored in this courtyard would surely make the Empress Dowager immediately recall a very bitter part of her own history as soon as she saw them. The facts contained in this history were nothing more than hardship, pain, terror, sorrow, struggle, and many heartbreaking tragedies; undoubtedly, this was a very painful memory. If it could be avoided, I think the Empress Dowager would never want to recall it often, but the pile of relics displayed before her eyes was the relics of her own husband - Emperor Xianfeng, and as soon as they caught her eye, they inevitably aroused her painful memories.

When she first entered the palace, she was selected along with sixteen other Manchu girls. All seventeen of them were beautiful and charming like flowers; but Xianfeng only fell in love with her alone, and soon officially made her a concubine, and she was the most favored in the palace.

Of course, the Empress Dowager was the most detailed and clear about Xianfeng's history; second only to Li Lianying; but at that time, Li Lianying was just a teenager, and he may not have had such a clear understanding. As for us - Guangxu, Empress Longyu, Consort Jin, and our eight female officials - each of us probably knew a little, all indirectly from listening to others; and among them, I heard the most! Because the Empress Dowager talked to me the most, and every time we talked, she couldn't help but recall the past, and there were many things in these past events that involved Xianfeng. (194)

Travels

A Visit to West Lake in Autumn

— Aisheng

I found the "Autumn Visiting Gathering" of the West Lake Butterfly Hotel in a newspaper advertisement. It said: The beauty of the red leaves surpasses the spring flowers. This kind of wording is not easy to find in advertisements. Moreover, the ticket, car, accommodation, food, and travel are all included. A two-day stay for a couple costs only thirty yuan, which is really a cheap and elegant thing, so we also became a member of the "Autumn Visiting Gathering."

We took a second-class train, and the tickets were prepared by the Butterfly Hotel. When we arrived at the Hangzhou Railway Station, we saw the "Butterfly" reception, wearing uniforms to greet us. At the same time, there were many members of the "Autumn Visiting Gathering," all in pairs. We estimated that they were at least couples, but we didn't recognize them.

We stepped onto the Butterfly Hotel's guest car from the station. The car body was very gorgeous and spacious, the size of a public bus, but the inside was equipped with sofas. I counted, and there were exactly six pairs including us. They probably all came to visit the autumn scenery, so they smiled at each other, because we would be traveling together tomorrow.

The Butterfly Hotel is a fine hotel located north of the Broken Bridge, facing the lake and mountains. It is not aristocratic, but very gorgeous and elegant, with a red corridor winding to the bedroom. There seemed to be many flowers and trees planted outside, and there were also thrushes and mynahs raised, because it was late, the birdcages were covered with cage covers, and the birds were not coming to welcome you as usual. We ate Western food for dinner, which had a very "Merry" flavor.

The next morning, the waiter gently knocked on the door and said: "Sir! It's half past seven." I quickly sat up. The room was full of crystal light, basking in the morning sun. The red corridor was outside the window, the lake was outside the red corridor, and the mountains were outside the lake, all like a painting, one layer after another shining into my eyes. I quickly woke her up, and after washing up, we had breakfast.

It turned out that there were more than just the six pairs who came on the same car as us to "Visit Autumn." There were also those who came in advance and joined temporarily. I saw that the route started with a car to Siyan Well, and I wanted to not take the car and go by boat. The hotel said: "You can," we have boats prepared. This "Autumn Visiting Gathering" is absolutely free. We got off the boat from the willows and went straight to South Lake. The morning sun shone on the water, like silver.

The boat could not go any further when it reached Chishan Wharf. We abandoned the boat and walked straight to the Stone House Cave. The boat was slower than the car as usual. When we arrived at the Stone House Cave, the people from the Autumn Visiting Gathering had already been there. Two sedan chairs were parked outside the gate, originally waiting for us to sit in. We did not enter the temple and sat in the sedan chairs and went straight to Yanhua Cave. Along the way, the shade of the pine trees, there were about a few chestnut trees and ginkgo trees, dyed with bright red and delicate yellow colors. I thought the Butterfly Hotel's advertisement was a bit exaggerated. Who knew that as soon as we reached the foot of the mountain, looking towards the South Peak, every tree, high and low, looked like it was drunk, and every tree was bright. The autumn colors were like brocade, really not empty words. In the flower hall, on the stone table under the shade of the trees, many people were eating and drinking there. It turned out that a table was prepared for two people, and no one had to be constrained by anyone. The Butterfly Hotel's owner's thoughtfulness and thoroughness of equipment made me have to admire at this time.

After dinner, we circled around the front and back of the mountain, all of which was autumn scenery. There was also a place under construction, building a house, which was said to be designed and built by the owner of the Butterfly Hotel, named "Butterfly Hidden Garden," because there was originally a "Butterfly Hidden Garden" here that had been abandoned for a long time, and now it is being rebuilt, and the name also coincides very well. Mr. Ma Yichu already had a couplet hanging in the cave, and I seemed to remember a sentence like "East is Su Shi West Butterfly Hidden."

We took sedan chairs from Yanhua Cave to Longjing to Li'an. The autumn colors along the way were ever-changing, and we couldn't see enough. The Nine Creeks and Eighteen Streams had already been paved with roads, and cars could drive straight in. The Butterfly's special car had been waiting for a long time. We were still eating Butterfly Hotel snacks on the snow-white tea cloth in front of the Jiuxi Tea Field. This time, it was a long table, and name cards were arranged in order to sit. We exchanged name cards with each other at the table. A day's tour just made us meet five or six friends who liked mountains and rivers, and we also left our names and praises on the signature book specially prepared by the Butterfly Hotel. The car arrived at Xucun at half past five. The planned tour of the Six Harmonies Pagoda was canceled, and we hurriedly boarded the gate train and went straight to Shanghai.

This kind of travel method is indeed worthy of attention and praise in the travel business. But this year's Autumn Visiting Gathering has ended. Revisit the old place, look forward to next year.

Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Morse Code Practice Machine for Both Telegraphy and Telephony

— Yi Zhi

If you are tired of playing with radio broadcast wavelengths, we should change our taste and try shortwave. Shortwave can be used for amateur communication, and it has super characteristics. You will be very interested in the experiment. We read O.S.T. and admire the activity of American amateurs, who often help the country's telecommunications traffic where it cannot reach; my country has a vast territory, and telecommunications traffic is still in its infancy, so many amateurs are needed to rise up and work for the country within the amateur range. To become an amateur, the first thing is to understand Morse code and be proficient in sending and receiving. This article introduces a Morse code practice machine for both telegraphy and telephony, which is also suitable for basic practice for beginners.

The Morse code practice machine is very easy to manufacture and costs very little. The required parts can all be replaced by those used in broadcast machines. Please refer to the attached diagram for the circuit. This machine is suitable for two people to practice. The intermediate distance can be arbitrarily tested, and it is connected with a double twisted wire of appropriate length. If the wire is too long and there is static interference, the outside of the wire must be isolated with a lead sheath. If it is for convenience, it is also possible to test using a single wire and ground circuit. In the figure, T is an audio frequency transformer. V is a vacuum tube, preferably of the 99 or 30 type, which is more economical to use. P is a receiver R is a 20-ohm current regulator. C is a fixed capacitor with a value from .005 to .08 megamicrofarads. If it is too large, the tone will be deep and blurry. KS is a key and switch. A is A battery, B is B battery, and the voltage is determined by the characteristics of the required vacuum tube. After matching the application parts and connecting them as shown in the figure, you can invite a comrade to test it.

During the test, if the sending operator at station B sends the message first, the switch at station A must be closed; when the sending operator at station B presses the key, the receiving operator at station A can receive a clear Morse code tone. After listening to the Morse code, party A immediately turns off the switch, presses the key to send the message, and after sending, closes the switch again, waiting for party B to reply. You can practice back and forth in this way.

This machine can also be used for telephony testing. When telephoning, the switch at station A must be closed first. The speakers at both stations each speak into a receiver and listen to a receiver. However, the voice must be heavy when speaking, otherwise the receiver diaphragm will not vibrate and the other party will hear nothing. The total impedance of the receivers used must be equal to achieve the best effect.

When this machine is used for sending test, attention must be paid to whether the oscillator is oscillating. Check whether the circuit is connected incorrectly. The second step is to exchange the wiring of the two transformers to test it.

Important Points Regarding the Structure of High-Frequency Amplifiers

— Li

(A) Capacitance due to high frequency

What is capacitance? The most obvious thing is a capacitor, two pieces close to each other, with capacitance. However, the grid and screen in the vacuum tube face each other, and the parallel arrangement of each circuit is a capacitor and has capacitance. The resistance generated by capacitance is called capacitive reactance. According to the formula, capacitive reactance is the frequency, and C is the capacitance. If the value of capacitance is constant, the degree of capacitive reactance depends on the size of the frequency. According to the formula, when the value of C is constant, the larger the value of f, the smaller the value of Xc. Therefore, it can be proved that the higher the frequency, the smaller the capacitive reactance, because the current on the radio frequency amplification circuit is high frequency, then the capacitive reactance in the circuit is reduced, so that the high frequency current is often easy to exceed the normal track, which is easy to cause various obstacles, such as oscillation, etc., making the radio reception chaotic. Therefore, when constructing an amplification receiver, the connecting lines used in each part are most afraid of being parallel and in close contact with each other. We must try to make the connecting lines perpendicular to each other to reduce the valley effect to the lowest limit.

(B) Position of the transformer

There are magnetic lines around the transformer. If it is an iron core, these magnetic lines will adhere to the iron core to form a magnetic circuit, and there will be less external magnetic force. However, because there is nothing to rely on for the magnetic lines of the air core transformer, there are many stray magnetic lines around it. It is especially severe at both ends of the coil. If several similar transformers are installed close to each other and connected to each other, they will interfere with each other, resulting in violent oscillation or reduced efficiency. We must remember not to touch other devices closely around the transformer when installing it. When several transformers are installed together, they must be perpendicular to each other or parallel to each other (each distance should be at least two inches or more). Some people advocate that the transformer should be installed at an oblique angle of 40 degrees to the ground plane so that it will not interact with the earth's magnetic force.

(C) Vacuum tube selection

Various vacuum tubes have the ability to amplify, but some vacuum tubes can be used for both detection and amplification, while others are specifically for amplification. Vacuum tubes for amplification are nothing more than hard tubes, which are better. The so-called hard vacuum tube is a glass bulb with an extremely high degree of vacuum so that the screen can withstand a relatively high voltage.

Because the amplification characteristics of vacuum tubes are very good, some people advocate that the amplification effect of vacuum tubes should be used purely on the amplifier. Although using a transformer can increase the amplification ability, it is not easy to get good results using a transformer with a large ratio, because the AC voltage received by the grid of the vacuum tube and the DC voltage it receives have certain limitations. A high-ratio transformer often causes the grid of the vacuum tube in the later stage to receive too high an AC voltage, resulting in abnormal current and oscillation action. Adding more vacuum tube stages is more likely to get satisfactory results.

(D) Adjustment of grid voltage

In a vacuum tube for amplification, a negative voltage of a C battery is often added to the grid. However, various vacuum tubes have their own characteristics and have mutual differences. The C voltage used for the grid cannot be generalized. The voltage of the C battery cannot be adjusted arbitrarily, so it is more convenient to adjust the grid voltage with a voltage divider. However, the voltage divider is directly connected to the two poles of the A battery group, and a suitable total switch must be used. When not in use, the current can be cut off to avoid unnecessary loss. Looking at the above four types, although they seem ordinary, we must pay attention to them when constructing a high-frequency amplifier. Therefore, the four types mentioned above are the main points of the construction of a high-frequency amplifier.

A Sensitive Short-Wave Single-Tube Radio

— Yong Yan

Using a No. 33 audio frequency amplification tube as a detector, its sensitivity is indeed much higher than that of an ordinary No. 30 vacuum tube. The long-short wave one-lamp radio described in this article uses a No. 33 vacuum tube as a feedback detector, so its sensitivity is indeed very superior; it has used ordinary broadcast radio antennas to receive short-wave broadcasts from the Soviet Union, the Netherlands, and the United Kingdom, as well as countless short-wave telegrams, and the volume is also very loud. Using its broadcast coil to listen to local telecommunications, the sound in the receiver is deafening. Therefore, it is introduced.

The circuit of this machine is not particularly unique, so it is very easy to construct, but you must be careful when making it in order to obtain satisfactory results. The machine uses a 50,000-ohm variable resistance to adjust the screen grid voltage of the No. 33 vacuum tube to control the feedback force, and the feedback effect is very stable. A total of four plug-in coils are used to receive each segment of wavelength, and the number of turns and wire number are as follows:

WavelengthL1L2Distance between L1 and L220 meters4 turns6 turns1/4 inch60 meters18 turns16 turns3/16 inch100 meters50 turns30 turns3/16 inchBroadcast segment1516 inches58 inches1/8 inch

Except for the L1 of the 20 and 60-meter segments, which uses a No. 26 double-yarn covered wire, the rest of the coils use a No. 26 enameled wire.

Its circuit is as shown in the attached diagram. The other parts in the diagram have been marked, so they will not be repeated here. All other parts should use high-quality products, otherwise it will affect its performance. A small 25-ampere-hour storage battery is best used for the A battery, or two dry batteries can be connected in series and the 66-ohm variable resistance can be reduced to 2 volts. 45 volts is enough for the B battery, and the maximum should not exceed 67 volts. The panel should use an aluminum plate (at this time, R must be insulated from the panel). All wiring should be short and straight, and all joints should be soldered with tin to obtain excellent results.

Two Improved Three-Circuit Crystal Radio Circuits

— Cai Rixin

The three-circuit is the best type of crystal radio, which is recognized by everyone. Indeed, its volume is much louder than that of an ordinary single-wire circuit, but the selectivity is not very good, which is very annoying: the author tested two methods for two weeks in order to increase its selectivity, and the result is the two methods in Figure 1 and Figure 2. (The figures are attached separately)

The results of these two circuits are both excellent. According to my observation after testing, Figure 2 is better than Figure 1. The filter in Figure 1 is not as effective as that in Figure 2. If you have a three-circuit crystal radio and feel that the selectivity is not good, you may want to try it. LL1L2, ordinary three-circuit coils are also acceptable.

L - No. 24 wire, wound 12 turns on the bead board.

L1 - No. 24 wire, wound 58 turns on the bead board.

L2 - No. 26 wire, wound 34 turns on the bead board.

L3 - No. 26 wire, wound 50 turns on a one-time diameter cylinder.

L4 - No. 26 wire, wound 22 turns on a cylinder, 7/8 inch apart.

L5 - No. 26 wire, wound 70 turns on a one-inch diameter cylinder, with a tap every ten turns.

C - 0.0003 megamicrofarad variable capacitor.

C - 0.00025 megamicrofarad variable capacitor.

D - Sensitive ore.

LL1L2 is installed on a three-circuit rack.

Filter Circuit

— Qing Zhao

If you want to design a radio with better selectivity, you must choose a good filter circuit to cope with it in order to remove unnecessary mixed sounds and increase its selectivity. The following figures A, B, and C show several excellent filter circuits. Figure A makes the LsCs circuit match the mixed sound wavelength and gives it a low-impedance path, so that unnecessary radio frequencies flow through it without flowing into the radio. In this way, the mixed sounds in the radio can be screened out. Figure B connects a small coil Ls between the antenna and ground ends of the radio, so that the LsCs circuit intersects with LC and is matched with the wavelength to be received, then LC is affected by the reaction of this circuit. As a result, the total impedance at the LC end is often the largest for the frequency to be received; however, for other frequencies, the value of its total impedance is low, so it can achieve the purpose of screening out mixed sounds. Figure C shows that the CsLs circuit is first matched with the mixed sound frequency, and the LtCt circuit is matched with the frequency to be received. Because the circuit is too complicated, it is not easy for unskilled people to adjust it.

Daily Difficulties and Remedies on the Radio

— Zhenmin

When using radios, we often encounter various difficulties, such as not receiving any signal, weak sound, noise, etc. The occurrence of these phenomena is not necessarily due to errors in the components of your radio. Sometimes, it is the result of neglecting a small part. Inexperienced people often panic when encountering the above-mentioned difficulties and replace components without considering the consequences, which often makes the radio even worse. After discovering a difficulty, it is best to carefully inspect each part of the radio and then make appropriate repairs. The following points are the most common difficulties encountered in daily radio use. Now, let's briefly explain their causes and remedies.

(1) No Reception (No sound in the earpiece or loudspeaker)

Cause Remedy

(A) Broken circuit Inspect the circuit, carefully solder the joints, and tighten the screws.

(B) Transformer burnout Use a voltmeter to measure the voltage of the primary and secondary coils. If there is no reading on the meter, the transformer must be replaced.

(C) Poor vacuum tube Replace with a better vacuum tube.

(D) Battery depleted Charge.

(E) Insufficient B voltage or incorrect connection Replace or swap connections.

(F) Rust on the battery terminals Test with an ordinary light bulb (small bulb), then replace.

(G) Damaged or burnt variable resistor Test first, then replace.

(H) Poor contact of the earpiece plug Test first, and try to increase the contact area.

(I) Poor contact of the vacuum tube socket Test first, and tighten the screws.

(J) Internal short circuit in the earpiece plug Remove the plug and test, then test with another plug, and then replace.

(K) Cracked earpiece wire Replace with another wire.

(L) Incomplete contact of the earpiece wire Remove the earpiece cover and try to tighten the wire end.

(M) Partial contact of the variable capacitor Test with a light bulb. If the light bulb lights up, then replace it.

(N) Antenna and ground wire not connected properly Carefully inspect the circuit and connect them tightly.

(2) Weak Reception

Cause Remedy

(1) Loose circuit contacts Inspect the circuit, tighten or re-solder.

(2) Rust or looseness at the antenna connection Clean it or re-solder it.

(3) Poor ground wire installation Test and re-install a better ground wire.

(4) Antenna in contact with branches or other conductors Inspect the antenna and try to remove this contact.

(5) Poor antenna insulation First connect the earpiece and C battery to the antenna and ground wire. If sound can be heard, the antenna must be replaced.

(6) Poor vacuum tube Replace with a better vacuum tube.

(7) Incomplete contact of the variable resistor Clean or replace.

(8) Battery exhausted Replace or charge.

(9) Defects in the earpiece or loudspeaker, or poor installation Install properly first. If the reception does not improve, it must be replaced.

(10) Improper configuration of radio frequency Pay close attention when tuning in. (Rotate the variable capacitor slowly)

(11) Radio waves absorbed by other steel structures Try to install a higher antenna. (To be continued)

Free Talk

The Yunnan-Vietnam Railway (Part 1)

— Li Qiao

The train exhaled a long plume of black smoke, floating behind the carriage like a messy braid, scattered into the woods by the gale, disappearing in a moment.

As if tired of walking, it panted hoarsely, darting from this mountain to that mountain, always clattering incessantly. The people sitting in the train were long since hypnotized by this rhythmic sound.

Outside the train window were towering, overlapping mountains, covered with dark, lush forests and green, velvety thatch. The train ran all day in this desolate, lonely mountain wilderness, along the torrents of the Fu Liang River. Sometimes, it burrowed into gloomy tunnels, piercing straight through the massive belly of the mountain - the journey was unexpectedly so arduous.

It was already three or four o'clock in the afternoon, and Hekou seemed to be arriving soon. Suddenly, a misty drizzle began to fall, the scene outside the window gloomy. Besides three young people who had never been out before and were marveling at the scenery, there was a group (about seven or eight) of Annamese women who were sleeping soundly with their heads bowed, wearing coffee-colored long gowns, their teeth stained black, chewing mouthfuls of bright red betel nut. They were probably exhausted from the long journey and the bumpy ride.

Because of the language barrier, we never spoke a word to them. These fair-skinned, red-lipped foreigners, with thick black braids wrapped around their heads and wooden shoes that clattered as they walked, constantly made us stare in amazement at their every move. Especially the way they smoked: squatting on the floor, their backs firmly against the wall, striking a match, putting the waterless pipe to their mouths, and inhaling forcefully - after three or four minutes, they would slowly open their mouths and exhale the smoke, as if they felt very refreshed. Their appearance really made us unable to help but laugh!

The three of us young people sat in the train, feeling gloomy, each with our heads down, thinking about our own affairs. Unexpectedly, the rain outside the window started to pour down, and the train was climbing a steep slope very slowly. We felt hungry.

The train came to a mountain hollow and was suddenly blocked by a large rock that had fallen from the top of the mountain, derailing the locomotive. Fortunately, this was a mountain hollow, and there was no danger - if we were traveling on a path thousands of feet high, with mountain streams rushing by the side of the road, then, my God, everything would be over!

The train derailed, and many workers came to repair it, but the stone lying under the wheels was so difficult to remove. It seemed that the train could not be repaired and started until tomorrow. However, in this uninhabited mountain hollow, what were we going to do?

It gradually got dark, and we became even more hungry - we looked at each other, anxiously smiling bitterly! Fortunately, at this time, those Annamese Bodhisattvas in the same carriage saw our plight and generously took out the rice they had brought with them and shared it with us.

This rice was really strange: wrapped tightly in tree leaves, like dumplings. Although we found it a bit unsanitary, we devoured it ravenously.

When we returned the bamboo-woven lunch boxes to them, we were still a bit unsatisfied, but we smiled sheepishly and handed them back, feeling unspeakable gratitude in our hearts!

It was already night, and everyone saw that we could only sleep in the carriage tonight. So we closed the carriage windows and doors to prevent wild animals from coming, opened our luggage, and leaned against it to sleep.

In the middle of the night, moonlight shone in through the cracks in the iron door, illuminating the carriage with a bright glow. Everyone thought it was dawn and hurried to open the iron door to take a look: the top of the mountain was covered with a layer of cloud-like white mist, connected to the white clouds in the sky. The clear light of the moon shone on the white mist, pure white, and indescribably beautiful - the trees and grass on the mountain... were quietly bathed in the moonlight, so gentle and lovely! As if they were already sound asleep. The still air was filled with a refreshing fragrance. In this vast and desolate place, only the distant, clear sound of the mountain spring was playing softly. It made people forget the hardships of the journey without realizing it.

Unfortunately, we only briefly enjoyed the wonderful night scene in this deep mountain for this one night. The next morning, we went to Lao Cai.

Emphasis on Characteristics

— Xinren

Emphasis on characteristics exists not only in art but also in natural science and social science. Natural scientists discovered that the main elements of water are hydrogen and oxygen, and further learned that water is a compound of two hydrogen and one oxygen, so they use H2O to represent water. However, actual water contains many other impurities besides these two elements. Social scientists study capitalist society and find out the main characteristics and laws: commodities, currency, etc. are the main characteristics, and panic, monopoly, war, and collapse are the main laws. They use these symbols to represent capitalist society; however, real capitalist society has infinitely complex phenomena. We cannot criticize the irreality of these scientific laws because of this abstract emphasis on characteristics.

Art is also like this, but it is not an abstract emphasis on characteristics but a concrete emphasis on characteristics. Anyone who asks Cervantes to find the real Don Quixote is a fool, because Don Quixote is a typical figure concretized by Cervantes, created through his work of emphasizing characteristics.

In short, emphasis on characteristics is necessary in both science and art. Without it in science, recognition cannot be concentrated; without it in art, the power to move art is lost. Especially the character of the characters in the work, if its characteristics are not emphasized, the loss is very great. Gladkov recently said: "…Modern huge images, guiding types, require writers to have great confidence…At this moment, a certain amount of idealization, a certain emphasis on the characteristics of personality, need not be feared." "Our focus should be…not portrait painting, but typical, not topical, but modern."

Ibsen's Creative Method

— Wang Jicong

(Part 1)

Mehring-Kautsky said: "Ibsen is an artist who denies all aesthetic forms. In the structure of his works, he is a classicist; in his deep poetic emotion, he is a romanticist. But if we further and spiritually study the personality of this poet, we may have to determine where he comes to a conclusion, that is, although he has various styles in form like Proteus (god of prophecy...), his fundamental nature is neither a naturalist, nor a classicist, nor a romanticist. In Ibsen's poems, social resistance and philosophical idealism, theoretically mixed with traditional social relations, exist." If we speak from the point of view of Ibsen's complexity as a great playwright, then Mehring-Kautsky's statement is of great significance. However, if we observe its complexity comprehensively, then we can know how Ibsen created and know what kind of literary school he belongs to. Because upon careful analysis, the creative methods of every great writer are almost very complex, but what determines their creative methods is only one thing - the content of the thoughts they want to express in their works; further, it is the era and society in which they are located. Ibsen is also the same. As long as we can start from this point and make a comprehensive and general observation, we can see the main trend of his creative method.

Needless to say, the so-called creative method is used to express certain things, certain thoughts and feelings. Leaving concrete things, leaving social thoughts and feelings, no creative method exists. Ibsen, who described the social phenomena of Norway in the second half of the nineteenth century, was an extreme individualist. His depiction of the social phenomena at that time was to express resistance to the society at that time under individualism. What about his creative method? Of course, it is used to express the social phenomena he wants to express, to express his individualism and spirit of resistance; in other words, it is derived from the content of his works. Therefore, first of all, in choosing themes, he cannot create with historical stories as themes like Goethe's "Faust" or Hugo's "Hernani". He must describe realistic social phenomena. His "A Doll's House", "Pillars of Society", "An Enemy of the People"…and other works all express real stories that can be found in Norwegian society at that time; the questions he raised in his creations about morality, religion, law, and even women are all realistic social issues: these are all obvious examples. Secondly, if Ibsen wants to resist the real society with the weapon of individualism, then he cannot abide by any formal rules, follow any principles of "character portrayal", like ordinary classicists; at the same time, he cannot be like the romanticists, fantasizing about things beyond reality and letting emotions run wild. For him, what is necessary is to vividly describe the living realistic social phenomena, because only in this way can the ugliness of reality be revealed (if that reality is ugly), and can his spirit of resistance be expressed. -- In this way, we can say that Ibsen is not a classicist, nor a romanticist, but should be attributed to the banner of naturalism. Ibsen himself once said in 1882: "The purpose of my writing books is to make every reader feel that everything he reads is fact." This is the argument held by general naturalists.

(Part 2)

However, the extreme individualist Ibsen's resistance to reality does not have a clear way out. He only violently attacks the morality, laws, and religion of the real society, and does not pay attention to the foundation of that real society that produces them. Therefore, he cannot go from resisting morality and law to a political outlet, which makes his general propaganda weak and ambiguous. As a result, the naturalist Ibsen put on the clothes of symbolism.

The so-called symbolism occurs when artists on the one hand want to resist reality, and on the other hand do not have clear ideas as a basis. Because there are no clear ideas, there will be no clear content, all there is is unconscious resistance; the result is of course no bright future, only "symbols", only sinking into the abyss of abstract "solipsism". Ibsen is like this. In all his plays, he is full of the spirit of resistance, but what is the result? They all end in a vague "purification of one's will", and even put all their efforts into longing for the heavens. For example, Nora's resistance to law, religion, and family in "A Doll's House" is for the sake of being a person; "Pillars of Society" has thoroughly exposed the hypocrisy of Norwegian citizens at that time, but the result tells us that personal freedom is more important than anything else; Dr. Stockmann in "An Enemy of the People" has also stubbornly fought against the old forces, but his central consciousness lies in "the strongest person in the world is the loneliest"; and Brand in "Brand" even puts his last efforts into longing for the heavens; others such as "The Lady from the Sea", "The Master Builder" and his last "When We Dead Awaken" all carry a strong smell of symbolism.

The strength of Ibsen's creation lies in his ruthless exposure of the evils of reality, his willingness to tell the truth, and his vivid depiction of the psychology and behavior of his petty-bourgeois protagonists. Some people say that he is an unparalleled petty-bourgeois psychologist, which is not without reason. I believe that anyone who studies the psychology of the petty bourgeoisie needs to read his works. In his plays, he often loves to use surprising scenes that people do not expect to grasp the psychology of general phenomena and to carry out his preaching. For example, in "A Doll's House", he initially portrays the protagonist Nora as very kind, like a "little dove", "little squirrel", making people not expect that such a person will resist, will leave home; but then he uses accidental events to stimulate her mind, making her show a firm spirit of resistance, pack her bags, and decide to leave. As a result, a surprising scene appears, the atmosphere of peace disappears, making the audience and actors as nervous as the author; so, taking this opportunity, Ibsen begins his preaching through Nora's mouth. -- Under such rules, Ibsen's creation has achieved great artistic effect. However, his symbolism has made his preaching ambiguous and weak, and thus has given his works great harm in art.

Silent Thought

— Bai Ying

Next to the small house, there is a lush locust tree. Although it is late autumn, not many leaves have fallen yet. The warm sunlight is tightly blocked, and the gloomy air sometimes gives me goosebumps all over my body.

Evening.

I sat under the window of this small house, watching the defeated, withered yellow locust leaves rolling down from the branches, falling on the ground, and being carried to the corner of the wall by the autumn wind.

--How poetic this is!

I thought silently. However, I am not a poet, I have neither the mood for appreciation nor any mysterious feelings. Only the past, like a fading dream, suddenly surfaced in my mind.

The first thing I thought of was the time five years ago when I lost my job and was at home in my hometown. At that time, I couldn't remember who was fighting whom, and soldiers were passing by every day, and no one in the village had escaped. - My hometown was originally in the deep mountains. It is said that except for the Boxer Rebellion, when foreign devils passed by once, it was this time. Foreign devils are really powerful, they kill and set fires, they do everything. So for the people there, it left the impression that "soldiers" are more terrible than "bandits." When soldiers come, the first thing to do is to escape. The old men would get angry when they saw that there was no one, and they would destroy things at will. In the end, not only were the people in the village gone, but also the things in the rooms were empty.

I remember the first time the soldiers hadn't arrived yet, my old father had already sent the people in the family to live at my aunt's house, and he and I were guarding the door at home. Sitting in the study - a study about the same size as my small house.

--They probably won't come today.

My father glanced at me.

--Xiao Fuzi just scouted out at Magouzhuang, there is no news at all.

--You might as well not come back! Living in Beijing, although there is nothing going on now, it is always more "alive" than at home. Now the road is so unsafe, when can you leave? In Beijing, you won't be as scared as you are at home!

--That's right!

--In the future, our life will be better... In another three years, your brother will also graduate...

My father showed a proud smiling face.

...

"Three years"? It's been five years now, hasn't it? "Life will be better" where is it? My old father has died because of excessive labor and worry. Although my younger brother has graduated, he is now unemployed at home. I once found him something to do. He said that the family is even harder to live these years and hopes that I will send some money back.

Money, where is there any to send! It was already not easy to maintain a small family with a few tens of dollars. What method do I have to arrange for my brother?

Father, brother, home, appeared before my eyes.

Dusk gradually ruled this world in misery.

Tomorrow (11)

— (Joseph Conrad) written, Wu Xiangyu translated

Captain Hagberd, annoyed at the mention of his clothes, took his shovel and went furtively inside; the two standing outside the door were startled by the sound of the door closing, followed by the sound of the door locking, and the echo of a feigned laugh inside.

After a short silence, the man said, "I don't want to disturb him." "What does all this mean? He's not very crazy."

"He's been worried about his lost son for a long time," Bessie said in a low, apologetic tone.

"Hey, I am his son."

"Harry!" she exclaimed - then fell into extreme silence.

"Know my name? Friend of the old man, eh?"

"He's our landlord," she murmured, while her hand gripped the iron railing.

"He owns both rabbit hutches, doesn't he?" Little Hagberd asked contemptuously, "That's what he thinks he can be proud of. Can you tell me, who is that fellow who's coming tomorrow? You must know part of the story. I tell you it's the old man's trick, nothing else."

She did not answer, she was helpless in the face of this insurmountable difficulty, and she was greatly surprised by this necessary, capable, and fearful event to explain. In this situation, she seemed to be involved in the madness.

"Ah! I am very sorry", she murmured.

"What's the matter?" he said calmly. "You don't have to worry about causing me discomfort. That might be someone else when he wasn't expecting it at all, it would be uncomfortable. I'm not afraid of being hanged; but when that person shows up tomorrow, there's going to be a show. I don't want the old man's property, but rights are always rights. I shall see I'm going to fight that bastard, no matter who he is!"

He had come closer, he was much taller than her on that side of the iron railing. He spied on her hands. He guessed she was trembling, which suddenly made him think she might be involved in the old man's little trick against him tomorrow. He had come just in time to spoil their trick. He was attracted to this idea - with great contempt for the trick he had seen through. But he had always been extremely tolerant of all women's tricks in his life. Her trembling was indeed quite severe, and her headscarf slipped off her head. "Poor devil," he thought. "Don't worry about that fellow. I dare say he'll change his mind before tomorrow. But how to deal with me? I can't spend my time idling in front of this door until tomorrow morning."

Shenbao Local Supplement

Commentary

The Terror of New Weapons

— Qi

Currently, all nations are anticipating the arrival of the "Future War." Indeed, the occurrence of each war seems inevitable. In this upcoming war, the "survival of the fittest" is naturally expected. However, what about the "fit"? They are unwilling to be easily devoured. Therefore, we must prepare our military force and fight to the death.

Speaking of military force, it doesn't seem to be a simple matter. The primary condition for military force is weaponry. Broadswords and spears are too old and impractical. Long guns can inflict fatal wounds. Alas, even long guns and machine guns are somewhat outdated. The needs of the times have surpassed their capabilities, and they are gradually being discarded.

"Create new weapons!" This slogan permeates the entire world.

The so-called new weapons must naturally devour all the past clumsy methods using the latest techniques. Thus, the "death ray" has been tested and succeeded. It is said that this "ray," when it touches a person, can numb their senses, like being drunk. Without any military force, people will obediently let you manipulate them.

However, even the "death ray" is insufficient because inventors have the obligation to "maintain secrecy." So, if a war truly breaks out, you send a ray at me, and I have nothing to reciprocate. It seems somewhat "unpleasant," unable to reenact the sky battles depicted in our "Investiture of the Gods" tales, which is a pity.

Nevertheless, times are changing. What is considered regrettable may show you some color after undergoing a certain process.

Perhaps coincidentally, I found this news item when I opened the evening paper!

"...Following the 'death ray,' there is now a 'death sound' as a new weapon. Death sound is a special sound wave that causes death. Scientists have studied its structural principles, stating that it is highly possible. Its principle is roughly based on the number of vibrations per second of sounds heard by ordinary humans. Above or below this number are sounds that humans cannot hear. Now, its vibration frequency is increased, turning it into an extremely high-short wave, an inaudible sound wave. Its power can cause those who hear it to go insane, and in severe cases, cause death..."

In the above research, it seems like a novel toy. However, when these different, new toys begin to unleash their power, the destruction and demise of humanity become possible.

Standing on the eve of great terror, before the devouring of new weapons, will the weak be left to be eliminated by the strong?

The Road

— Xu Xizhen

It was early winter when A’Hu followed his second uncle and others on a small boat to Shanghai for the first time.

Walking on the streets of the metropolis, the thin lined jacket and trousers he wore rustled loudly in the cold wind. He shivered, but didn't feel cold. "Looking at the countless stores with their big sale flags and colorful electric lights, he couldn't help but smile. Thinking about the small shops in his hometown town, with their red paper strips crookedly pasted on the yellowish glass, saying 'Special Clearance Sale', it was really annoying.

In the evening, the second uncle found a cousin who worked as a rickshaw puller in the city, and he took them to stay in an empty attic of a relative. Thus, they arrived in Shanghai.

The next morning, the second uncle took A’Hu out to stroll around the streets (actually, to familiarize themselves with the roads). At a street corner, they heard a character reader shouting:

"Want to try it out? See if it's accurate on the spot!

Four copper coins, to ask about the ups and downs of the year, business fortune, and also to ask about finding business and switching business!"

"Finding business and switching business!" That touching advertisement struck the heart of this old "businessman" from the countryside with a bang, as if attracted by an irresistible force. He couldn't help but stop in front of the character reading stall and resolutely took out eight copper coins to ask about "business fortune" for himself and A’Hu.

The result was surprisingly joyful: both of them had great fortune in their years and smooth sailing in all their endeavors!

On the way back, the second uncle actually smiled. (According to A’Hu's memory, it was the first time he had seen the second uncle smile so happily since the Dragon Boat Festival.) He said repeatedly: "A’Hu, I said heaven never blocks all paths, Shanghai is good after all, we have smooth sailing," listen to that!"

He hid that "auspicious good omen" tightly in his heart like a treasure. On the afternoon of the third day, he went to find his cousin who was a rickshaw puller again: "Brother, you are familiar with Shanghai's market, please think of a way for me. Is there any 'road' to business?"

But the answer was more shocking than the character reader's "smooth sailing" to the second uncle. "Hey, you really take everything so easily! Does Shanghai have so many 'businesses' waiting for you? What can you do? Do labor? You don't seem to have the strength of an ox. Besides, people stronger than you are still begging for food in Shanghai. Do business? The huge stores are on sale and still no one comes to trade, 'everyone's closing down'."

But although the words were shocking enough to the second uncle, they didn't convince him. He didn't believe that such a good Shanghai didn't have his "road."

He himself was over sixty years old. He had been running a small shop in his hometown for at least ten years, right? But he had never seen such a year: "Hard" goods like matches, soap, and towels—daily necessities—no one wanted. In fact, no one even bought white rice in the rice shop! He, the second uncle, had experienced this himself and knew it very well.

After talking with his cousin for a day, he believed that the words "smooth sailing" were a bit unreliable: even A’Hu couldn't pull a rickshaw: pulling a rickshaw required a guarantor, which the second uncle had never even dreamed of.

And A’Hu, such a strong young man, was also stunned.

He wanted to set up a small stall on the street with A’Hu with the small goods he had brought out from the closed-down "Jing Guang Grocery" shop in his hometown, but it was said that it couldn't be done: he had to pay stall fees first. Thus, these few goods were useless. Watching the two yuan and more cash he had brought with him dwindle day by day, the second uncle was so anxious. Finally, he entrusted his cousin to sell some daily necessities cheaply to a Jinghuo store. When he got five yuan, his cousin said: "There's no road anywhere this year. Shanghai is a tiger's mouth, it's very scary. I advise you to go back to your hometown and suffer through the winter."

Standing there, he was at a loss, not hearing anything, only hearing one sentence: "There's no 'road' anywhere this year."

The Wood-Chopping Old Man

— Yafei

"Hunchbacked old man, beard all loose, sees a good lady, eyes are just two slits." When he went out to chop wood every day, a group of wild children would chase after him and shout this, but he wasn't angry. He always turned around and smiled at them, saying: "Naughty little kids, I'll tell your mothers later to punish you."

He was very kind, and because he was kind, many children wanted to play with him. He was sixty-eight years old this year, but he was still very strong. He said himself: "Not to boast, four or five young men can't rattle me." But I have never seen him fight or get angry with anyone. People always greeted him with a smile.

I knew his surname was Xin, but there was no Xin in the Book of Family Names. As for his name, I didn't know it, but I heard people call him Old Man Changmao; that was probably his name. But I remembered that the soldiers during the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom were called Changmao, so his name might be a nickname! In our village, he had no seniority, and everyone, old and young, called him Old Man Changmao. He, on the other hand, called older women "sister-in-law," young ones "bride," unmarried ones "girl," and girls "little sister." He called men the same way, "brother," "younger brother," "little brother," "little kid." When he met someone wearing a long gown, he would call them "sir" or "young master."

He lived in a tomb estate house belonging to the Mi family, making a living by chopping wood all year round. In the two small plots of land beside the house, he planted two gardens full of lush green vegetables. He didn't observe any holidays or festivals, and when something happened in the village, he would take on the task of providing firewood, but he never haggled over the amount of the reward, so people always sent him some cakes, rice dumplings, vegetables, and other food to eat during the New Year and festivals. He also liked to drink, but not much. A hundred copper coins worth of raw grain liquor could last him at least two days, but he couldn't do without it. He also smoked a few pipes of dry tobacco, which were probably his only hobbies in life.

Speaking of his life, he got up every morning at daybreak, smoked a pipe of dry tobacco, put on his jacket, and patrolled the vegetable garden to see if anyone had come to steal vegetables. After returning, he made breakfast and went up the mountain to chop wood. He didn't come back for lunch because it took too much time to travel back and forth, so he always brought some steamed buns or sweet potatoes to satisfy his hunger, so that he could chop a few more bundles of firewood, and he would return when the sun went down. When he got back, he carried water to water the vegetables, and when everything was settled, he would stir-fry the cold rice until it was hot and eat it, and then lie in bed, still thinking about what he should do tomorrow.

One day, because it was raining, I was idle, so I went to find him to talk. When I got to his house, he was just making straw sandals. We talked for a long time, and he told me how fierce the Changmao during the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom were, how the refugees suffered, and how cruel the government soldiers were. He was still young at that time, and he escaped with his father. His mother was killed by the Changmao! He also said:

"My father escaped to this place and worked for others, and slept here with me at night. I still sleep here now. Because I like to tell stories about the Changmao, people call me Changmao. Actually, my real name is A’Mao."

Winter Overcoat

— Jing

The gray-black floating clouds, like old tattered cotton wadding, spread over the entire sky, freezing like ice, with not a trace of blue cracks visible. The sky was indeed so low that it seemed to cover people's heads.

The early winter cold wind, like a knife, roared straight down from the tops of the withered yellow trees, rustling as it swept down the fallen leaves. Along the sidewalks of the road, sparse pedestrians hurried back and forth, shrinking their necks as they were blown by the sand-laden cold wind. Although the drummers on the upper floors of the department stores were still desperately blowing and drumming, the front doors were deserted, with not a single customer in sight. Only the "Peach Blossom River" song transmitted from upstairs lulled the clerks into a somewhat sleepy state, tilting their heads and yawning. The streetlights standing by the roadside, emitting a dim yellow glow, weakly and lifelessly,

Mutual Use

Page 23

In the winter twilight, they also seemed to feel the cold weather, constantly shivering.

"The weather is gradually getting colder, and it may snow soon. It's impossible to go without an overcoat." As He Lian turned into that quiet little road, he felt the severity of the cold wind especially keenly, his hands and feet freezing cold and numb. He muttered to himself privately.

Thus, He Lian thought of his winter overcoat stored in the pawnshop.

At the same time, he also recalled an incident he had encountered yesterday when he went to his friend's house for a banquet—an incident that, when he thought about it now, still made his thin, pale face suddenly flush with a red cloud. His heart was as uncomfortable as if many small insects were crawling and biting inside. At that time, he really didn't have the mood to enjoy the delicious dishes:

When He Lian stepped into his friend's house, the luxuriously furnished living room was already full of guests. Thus, his friend introduced him to everyone. When he shook hands with a young lady, he felt that the lady, upon touching his cold palm, shivered involuntarily, and goosebumps appeared on her face covered with rouge. This really made him so ashamed that he wished there was a hole he could immediately crawl into. His friend also seemed to realize something and said to him privately:

"Lian, haven't you felt cold these days? Why don't you wear your overcoat?"

Perhaps the sad living conditions of wanderers are not well known to certain gentlemen with inheritances, just as in the philosophy of wealthy people who live secluded lives, they don't believe that poor people are so impoverished that they don't even have food to eat. But who doesn't want face?

"Well, because I went out at noon, and the sunshine was very warm then..." Saying this, another guest arrived, and his friend was busy entertaining them, so He Lian finally left the rest of the sentence unfinished.

"The winter overcoat must be taken out." When He Lian stepped out of his friend's door, braved the biting cold wind, and got on a rickshaw back home, he had already decided on the way to send the two sets of summer clothes in his trunk to the pawnshop tomorrow, and then take out the winter overcoat.

Mother and Wife

— No

Mother - A sickly mother.

Wife - A newlywed wife.

He - The mother's son, the wife's husband, a young man in his early twenties who is not yet self-reliant.

His mother loves him, and his wife loves him too. He happily accepts these two different kinds of love.

He has both fish and bear's paw. But such a heavenly environment is, in fact, not allowed. The mother loves him, not his wife; the wife loves him, not his mother. If the mother and wife could both love the house and crow, then his happiness could be maintained.

But women are, after all, women - their love is intuitive, and they do not consider that the pain of their quarrels will be added to the person they love.

Before her illness, the mother was gentle. But years of sickness have tempered her temperament into irascibility.

As for the wife? She is loyal to her husband. As long as her reasons are correct, she will do her best to defend herself against the other party's attacks.

But the mother, whose irascibility has been forged by illness, constantly wants to fulfill what she considers her inherent authority as a mother-in-law. Therefore, she sees her wife's defense as resistance, as disobedience, and feels that she cannot back down without teaching her a lesson.

Thus, the bubble of happiness has burst.

Who is to blame? The wife, she is not wrong; the mother, she is the creator of her own situation!

The rope of pain tightly binds him. He has no strength to mediate and dare not protect either side.

Such an unfortunate crisis is brewing, brewing, and finally one day it erupts -

In a ward on the third floor of XX Hospital, a young woman who has taken poison and a panicked young man are brought in. The man anxiously asks the doctor who is performing the surgery:

- Can she be saved?

His pitiful gaze is like that of a criminal begging for mercy in court.

- Too late!

The doctor puts down the needle and replies without any expression.

Like a death sentence, he collapses on his wife's body, his hands tightly grasping her stiffening fingers, calling his wife's name in a heartbreaking manner as if summoning her soul:

- Lijing! Lijing! Lijing!

Tears fall drop by drop on the pale face of the woman he loves, the face of a wife lingering at the gate of life and death! He hopes that her tightly closed mouth will move and be able to say a few last words to him.

But everything has been decided by fate. His wife's eyelids only lift slightly once and she can no longer say anything.

Dazed, as if his soul has been taken away by his wife, an unusual shock pierces his heart. The shadow of his wife floats up as soon as he closes his eyes. He remembers when he left this morning, his wife very seriously said goodbye to him; but who would have thought? At such a young age (twenty years old), such a small incident (inevitable bickering between mother-in-law and daughter-in-law), to take that road with such determination.

Thinking of his wife's past kindnesses, thinking of his wife's current tragic death, he really wants to avenge her, even at the cost of his own life. But needless to say, it was the mother who caused the incident - a mother whose irascibility had been forged by illness! So this thought had to be forever buried in his heart.

Who is to blame? This chasm between mother-in-law and daughter-in-law!
